### MILESTONE SUMMARY — Pipeline (operations opener)
The operational task queue shipped end-to-end: scoped `/api/v2/tasks` list/stats/export (TASK-level scope composition — the one seam, now with `taskPredicate` grain), assignment hardening (OCC + scope-guarded writes closing the unguarded-assignment IDOR; append-only `task_assignment_history`; eligibility = unit.worker_role ∩ hierarchy ∩ territory; intersection pool + per-row bulk-assign on ONE write path), and the `/pipeline` workbench (Universal DataGrid + bucket bar + bulk-assign dialog). Every slice: fresh-DB `pnpm verify` green (final api 489 · sdk 81 · logger 4 · Playwright 81), Audit Panel PASS (slice-3 must-fix `q`→search applied + spec-pinned), live browser actions performed + persisted.
**Open carries (durable):** version-bump TOCTOU ratchet for future task status writers (mobile start/complete) · case purge path must handle the history immutability trigger · f_status-into-stats nuance (status not exposed as header filter by design) · ILIKE %/_ escaping (platform-wide) · ops cases export · PDF/≥10k export job tier.

## Audit Panel — Case-creation dispatch-fields slice (2026-06-11)

Reviewed: UNCOMMITTED working tree (ADR-0023) — migration `db/v2/migrations/0037_case_task_dispatch_fields.sql` (untracked); `packages/sdk/src/{cases,auth}.ts`; api `modules/cases/{repository,service,controller(unchanged)}.ts`, `modules/auth/repository.ts`; FE `apps/web/src/features/cases/CaseCreatePage.tsx`; tests. Gate: `tsc --noEmit` green on api-v2 + sdk + web-v2.

**VERDICT: FLAG** — security & DB are sound; one real correctness gap (F1, addTasks unmapped UNIQUE/FK → 500) and three minor flags. Nothing blocks; F1 is a `try/catch` away and worth fixing in this slice since it is the exact concurrency failure mode called out.

### Findings

- **F1 · MEDIUM · `apps/api/src/modules/cases/repository.ts:258-307` (addTasks)** — the method returns `withTransaction(...)` with **no try/catch**, unlike sibling `create` (`:192-195` maps `23503`→`INVALID_REFERENCE`). A `task_number` UNIQUE collision (`23505`) or a stale `applicant_id`/unit FK (`23503`) therefore propagates raw → global handler → **500**, not a 4xx. This is the task_number-race failure mode. *Recommendation:* wrap the tx the same way `create` does and map `23505`→`AppError.conflict('TASK_NUMBER_CONFLICT')` (retryable) and `23503`→`INVALID_REFERENCE`. Small, in-scope.

- **F2 · LOW · migration `0037:20-22` vs SDK `packages/sdk/src/cases.ts:58` (callingCode)** — DDL adds `case_applicants.calling_code varchar(40)` **nullable** (ADR table lists it without NOT NULL; backfill + repo always generates, so never null in practice), but the SDK types `CaseApplicant.callingCode: string` (non-null). Contract claims a guarantee the DB does not enforce. *Recommendation:* either `SET NOT NULL` after backfill (consistent with the other dispatch cols, all NOT NULL) or type it `string | null`. Prefer NOT NULL — it is owner-required dispatch data.

- **F3 · LOW · service `apps/api/src/modules/cases/service.ts:69-75` (addTasks)** — `caseApplicantIds` + `allUnitsEnabled` run as two **separate** queries *before* the insert tx (TOCTOU window: an applicant/unit could be deleted between check and insert). Acceptable here — applicants/units are not deleted in this flow and the FK + the F1 mapping would catch a true race — but note it; the airtight version validates inside the tx. No change required this slice.

- **F4 · LOW · `apps/api/src/modules/auth/repository.ts:148` + sdk `auth.ts:27` (phone on /me)** — `authUserById` now SELECTs `phone`; it flows through `svc.me`/`login` (`service.ts:149,131`) into the AuthUser payload. **Safe**: `/me` returns the caller's OWN record (self-data, like email/username already there); no other-user exposure path (`listSessions`-by-id uses a different shape). Prefill is correct. Noted for completeness, not a defect.

### Dimension notes (PASS)

- **SECURITY ✓** — all values parameterized; `task_number` is built in SQL via `(SELECT case_number ...) || '-' || $7::text` (bound param, not string interpolation) — no injection. **IDOR airtight**: `service.addTasks` validates every `applicantId ∈ caseApplicantIds(caseId)` → `INVALID_APPLICANT` (test `cases.api.test.ts` "rejects a task targeting an applicant from another case"); the DB FK is only `→case_applicants(id)` (cross-case at the DB), so the *service* check is the real guard and it is present + tested. RBAC unchanged (`routes.ts:13-14` both `CASE_CREATE`). `appendAudit` actor = `userId` (the create caller) — correct. **Mobile dispatch contract (audit §3) intact**: purely additive columns + derived-at-dispatch model per ADR; no `/sync` shape touched here.
- **DB ✓** — migration is `BEGIN/COMMIT`, all `IF NOT EXISTS` / `DROP CONSTRAINT IF EXISTS` → **idempotent + forward-only**; NOT NULL cols backfilled before constraint (placeholder `'0000000000'`, `''`, primary-applicant for `applicant_id`, computed `task_number`). FK + `idx_case_tasks_applicant` + `uq_case_task_number (case_id, task_number)` correct; CHECKs (priority, extended status) correct. `calling_code varchar(40)` vs generated `CC-<base36 epoch>-<8hex>` = **20 chars** → comfortable margin.
- **API ✓** — `AddTasksInput = z.input` (callers omit `trigger`/`priority` defaults) while the **server applies defaults** via `AddTasksSchema.parse(input)` in `service.ts:68` — correct split (test asserts `priority==='MEDIUM'` default persists). `task_number` ordinal = `count(*) + i` inside the tx → correct continuation across multiple batches for sequential adds. `calling_code` generated per-applicant inside the create tx (`repository.ts:182`). Error mapping present for create; **gap = addTasks (F1)**.
- **CODE QUALITY ✓** — magic numbers named in the business layer (`CC_PREFIX/CC_RAND_LEN/BASE36`, `MAX_TASKS/MAX_ADDRESS/MAX_TRIGGER/MIN_CONTACT`); surgical (shared `TASK_VIEW_COLS/FROM` dedup is a clean, in-scope refactor of the two task SELECTs the slice had to touch anyway); no dead code; snake SQL / camel TS consistent. **TOCTOU ratchet**: no new task *status writer* added (status enum extended, but no start/complete/finalize here) → ratchet not yet due; carry stands.

### task_number-race verdict

**Real but low-likelihood; map it, don't serialize it.** `seq = (SELECT count(*) WHERE case_id=$1)` then insert at that ordinal, all inside `withTransaction`. Two concurrent `addTasks` on the SAME case can both read the same `count(*)` (READ COMMITTED) and try to insert the same `task_number` → `uq_case_task_number` **catches the collision** (no duplicate row, no silent corruption — the index does its job). The defect is purely the **failure mode**: with no catch (F1) the loser's `23505` becomes a **500** instead of a clean 409/retry. Risk is low — a case is just-created by one operator and concurrent add-tasks on one case is rare — so this is **acceptable to ship**, but the fix is trivial (one try/catch mirroring `create`) and removes the only 500 path in the slice. **Recommend fixing in THIS slice** (F1). Not a blocker.

---

## Audit Panel — Mobile sync read-model slice (2026-06-11)

**Slice:** `apps/api/src/modules/sync/{repository,service,controller,routes}.ts` + `__tests__/sync.api.test.ts`, `packages/sdk/src/sync.ts`, wiring in `http/app.ts` + `sdk/src/client.ts`/`index.ts`. Read-only `GET /api/v2/sync/download` serving the unmodified field app the locked v1 dispatch contract.

**OVERALL VERDICT: PASS (1 FLAG to fix in-slice — F1 malformed-timestamp 500).** Security leak-proof, contract byte-verified against the device's own `sync.schema.ts`, COUNT exact, no N+1. One robustness defect and two dormant carries.

### Findings

- **F1 · MEDIUM · `service.ts:67-69` → `repository.ts:73` (`cutoff.toISOString()`)** — `SyncDownloadQuerySchema.lastSyncTimestamp` is `z.string().optional()` (sync.ts:88) — any string passes Zod. A malformed value (`?lastSyncTimestamp=garbage`) yields `new Date('garbage')` = Invalid Date; `cutoff.toISOString()` then throws `RangeError: Invalid time value`, which is NOT a ZodError/AppError → global handler (`app.ts:99-100`) maps it to **500 INTERNAL**, not a clean 400. The device always sends a well-formed ISO string (`SyncDownloadService.ts:57`), so this is not a live break — but a bad client / probe gets a 500 instead of a validation 400. **Recommend:** tighten the schema to `z.string().datetime()` (Zod emits a 400 ZodError), OR guard the coercion in the service (`Number.isNaN(cutoff.getTime())` → `throw AppError.badRequest`). Trivial, removes the only 500 path in the slice.

- **F2 · LOW (dormant) · `repository.ts:76` (`taskScopePredicate`) vs design "never narrows below the assignment"** — For FIELD_AGENT as wired today the claim HOLDS: role hierarchy mode = SELF (`0033_roles.sql:53` → `userIds=[self]`), and the ONLY wired dimensions are PINCODE + AREA, both **EXPAND** (`0034_scope_dimensions.sql:60-61`); **no RESTRICT dimension exists for FIELD_AGENT**. The composed predicate is therefore `(assigned_to=ANY([self]) OR cs.created_by=ANY([self]) OR expand-legs)` with NO trailing AND-RESTRICT leg → can only ADD via OR, never subtract. ANDed under the leading `ct.assigned_to=$1`, the net is exactly `assigned_to=self`. **Latent risk:** if an admin ever wires a RESTRICT dimension onto FIELD_AGENT, `composeScopePredicate` appends `AND restrictLeg`, and a RESTRICT dimension with zero user assignments emits `= ANY('{}')` → FALSE (fail-closed by design) → it WOULD hide *validly-assigned* tasks (or all of them). Accepted-by-design today; flag so a future RBAC wiring change to FIELD_AGENT triggers a re-test of down-sync visibility. Not a blocker.

- **F3 · INFO · `repository.ts:84-89` (ORDER BY)** — `idx_case_tasks_assigned (assigned_to)` exists (`0010_cases.sql:71`) and is the selective driver (one device's tasks = tens/low-hundreds). No composite index covers `ORDER BY COALESCE(ct.updated_at, cs.updated_at) ASC, cs.id ASC`, so Postgres sorts the small filtered set in memory. For per-device cardinality this is fine — **no index needed**. Watermark `COALESCE(ct.updated_at, cs.updated_at) > $2` is non-sargable on the COALESCE (can't use a plain `updated_at` index), but again the assigned_to filter already reduces to a tiny set, so it's a post-filter, not a scan. Acceptable.

### Verdict (a) — assigned_to=self scope decision: **PASS (leak-proof).**

`ct.assigned_to = $1` is the leading, unconditional AND-term of the WHERE (`repository.ts:75`); `$1 = actor.userId` from the authorize()-guarded `req.auth.userId` (`controller.ts:9`), never client-supplied. A device can NEVER receive a task whose `assigned_to ≠ self`: the composed scope seam is ANDed and (as wired) can only OR-broaden within the already-pinned assignment, so it cannot leak another user's task. The defense-in-depth seam without sub-assignment narrowing is **defensible vs MOBILE_API_COMPATIBILITY's "compose the scope seam" clause** — the seam IS composed (taskScopePredicate is called), it just doesn't cap below the contract filter, which is the correct read for a per-device dispatch feed (a territory change must not strand a validly-assigned task on the agent's phone). Cross-user leak via joins: NONE — all joins are many-to-one on PK (`case_id/applicant_id/verification_unit_id/client_id/product_id` FKs, NOT NULL where inner-joined; creator/assignee LEFT JOIN on PK), so no row from the page belongs to another case/user. SQL injection: NONE — every value is a bound `$n` param (userId, cutoff.toISOString(), scope arrays via composeScopePredicate's `params.push`, limit/offset); no string interpolation of user input. Permission gate `case.view` correct (FIELD_AGENT holds exactly CASE_VIEW, `permissions.ts:73`); unauth → 401 (tested, `sync.api.test.ts:230-232`; controller fail-closes `AppError.unauthenticated()` if `req.auth` ever absent). Endpoint leaks nothing beyond the agent's own dispatch (customer name/phone/address/client/product/trigger are exactly what the field agent must see to perform the visit). Only caveat is F1 (malformed timestamp → 500, not a leak).

### Verdict (b) — contract fidelity vs v1: **PASS (byte-verified against the device schema).**

Verified `service.ts toMobileTask` + the envelope against the device's actual consumer (`crm-mobile-native/src/api/schemas/sync.schema.ts` + `src/sync/SyncDownloadService.ts`), not just the TS interface:
- **Hard requirements met:** device `MobileCaseSchema` requires `id: z.string().min(1)` (← `r.id`, task uuid, always present) and `caseId: z.union([string,number])` (← `r.caseId` = case_number string; device tolerates string, asserted in test:158). `data.cases` required array (service sets it). ✓
- **Envelope exact:** device reads `response.data` (`SyncDownloadService.ts:61`) then `data.{cases,revokedAssignmentIds,deletedTaskIds,deletedCaseIds,conflicts,attachmentChanges,syncTimestamp,hasMore,nextCursor}` — EVERY name present in `service.ts:79-90` with matching types; `cases === changes` (same array ref, test:148). Placeholder arrays `[]` match v1's wire. nextCursor `string|null`, hasMore bool. ✓
- **Phantom fields:** `addressCity/State/Pincode = ''` emitted exactly as v1 (no source columns) — device stores them as-is; test asserts `''` (test:163-164). ✓
- **Dead fields:** `customerEmail`, `latitude`, `longitude` correctly OMITTED — v1 never populated them either; device binds them to NULL at rest (`SyncDownloadService.ts:532-533` reads `task.customer_email/latitude/longitude` → undefined → null). Byte-identical to v1. ✓
- **Execution fields** (`completedAt/inProgressAt/savedAt/verificationOutcome/formData/attachments`) emitted undefined/`[]`/`false`/`0` — same as v1's wire for a freshly-assigned task; device has safe defaults. `isRevoked = status==='REVOKED'`; the device separately normalizes `SUBMITTED_FOR_REVIEW→COMPLETED` at ingestion (`SyncDownloadService.ts:441`), same division of labour as v1. ✓
- **Nothing the device reads is MISSING** from the payload (the device INSERT at `SyncDownloadService.ts:529-539` binds every column from `task.*` with null-coalescing; only the two identity fields are mandatory, both always present).

Accepted-by-design items CONFIRMED (not re-flagged): `revokedAssignmentIds=[]` until task-revoke lands; execution fields empty because v2 doesn't store them; `caseId` = string case_number (device accepts string|number). All correct.

---

## Audit Panel — B-7.1 background-job spine (ADR-0030) (2026-06-15)

**Slice (UNCOMMITTED working tree):** NEW `db/v2/migrations/0050_jobs.sql`, `docs/adr/ADR-0030-background-jobs.md`, `platform/jobs/{index,repository}.ts`, `modules/jobs/{service,controller,routes}.ts` + `__tests__/jobs.api.test.ts`, `packages/sdk/src/jobs.ts`. MODIFIED `http/app.ts` (notifier injection + route mount), sdk `{client,client.test,index,notifications}.ts`. Gate: `tsc --noEmit` GREEN on api-v2 + sdk. Worker/BullMQ/Valkey, export/import processors, and FE (`useBackgroundJob`/Hexagon/DataGrid-enqueue) are DEFERRED to later slices by design.

**OVERALL VERDICT: FLAG (clear to commit after F1).** Scope is minimal and on-spec; no frozen-standard violation. One real robustness deviation (F1 — unhandled rejection on the notifier, fixable with the in-repo `notifySafely` precedent) plus two INFO doc-vs-code notes. Nothing blocks.

### Findings

- **F1 · MEDIUM · `apps/api/src/http/app.ts:67` (`void notificationService.notify(n)`)** — the injected `JobNotifier` fires the bell insert as `void notificationService.notify(n)` with **NO `.catch`**. `notify` is `async` (`modules/notifications/service.ts:32` → `repo.insert` → DB round-trip) and CAN reject (transient DB error). Unlike every OTHER producer in this codebase — `cases/service.ts:35` defines `notifySafely` precisely to wrap `notificationService.notify(input).catch(...)` — this call swallows the promise with `void`, so a rejection becomes an **unhandledRejection**. Worse, it fires from `runJob` AFTER the HTTP response (no request context, no global error handler to absorb it) → in prod with `unhandled-rejections=strict` it can crash the process. *Fix:* mirror the established pattern — `setJobNotifier((n) => { void notificationService.notify(n).catch((e) => logger.error('job notify failed', { error: ... })); });` (or reuse `notifySafely`). Trivial, in-scope, removes the only unhandled-promise path in the slice.

- **F2 · INFO · `platform/jobs/index.ts:130` vs ADR-0030 §3 / mig `0050:4` ("on `setImmediate` after the HTTP response is sent")** — the in-process runner is NOT scheduled on `setImmediate`/`nextTick`; `enqueue` awaits the PENDING `insert`, then fires `runJob(...)` as a **floating promise** (tracked in `inFlight`, with a `.catch` at :130-132 — so no unhandled rejection here) and returns the PENDING row immediately. Functionally equivalent for the producer (request returns with PENDING; the run executes concurrently with response serialization, not strictly "after"), but the doc/comment overstate the ordering. No behavioural defect; align the wording or add the `setImmediate` when the producer call sites land. Not a blocker.

- **F3 · INFO · doc-vs-code: `GET /jobs/:id/result-url` (ADR §4) + `JobResultUrl` (sdk `jobs.ts:31`) are declared but UNROUTED** — `routes.ts` mounts only `GET /` + `GET /:id`; no `result-url` controller/route exists, and `JobResultUrl` has no SDK client method. **Correct scope call** — the presigned download belongs to the export-processor slice (B-13, the type even says so). The type sitting ahead of its route is harmless forward-prep (precedent: `LocationCapture*`, `export.ts`). Noted so a reviewer doesn't mistake the missing route for an omission.

### Dimension notes (PASS)

- **SCOPE ✓** — minimal spine: table + seam + read-only own-tray API + SDK contract + one notifier wire + tests. NO producer calls `enqueue` yet (grep-confirmed: only the platform definition + the test) → export/import 413/`*_TOO_LARGE` paths UNCHANGED, nothing half-built leaks in. No BullMQ import (lazy, deferred). No FE. Speculative surface limited to the two F3 forward-prep declarations (accepted).
- **SECURITY / RBAC ✓** — **own-user scoped = identity not permission, correct & safe** (matches notifications precedent, ledger 2026-06-11 sync slice reasoning). `routes.ts` mounts NO `authorize(perm)` — every read filters `WHERE created_by = $actor`: `getOwned(id, userId)` returns null for a non-owner → controller `AppError.notFound()` (IDOR-safe, tested :93-98); `listOwned`/`countOwned` both pin `created_by = $1` = `req.auth.userId` (never client-supplied; `requireUserId` 401s if absent, tested :105-108). `:id` UUID-shape-guarded (`controller.ts:12,27`) → bad value is a clean 404, not pg `22P02`→500 (tested :100-103). `payload` (job input — may carry filters) is EXCLUDED from `READ_COLS` (`repository.ts:9`) → never returned to the client; only `JobView` (no payload) is exposed. No cross-user join. **No injection** — every value bound `$n`; the only interpolated tokens in `listOwned` (`p.sortColumn`/`p.sortOrder`) come from `resolvePage(rawQuery, JOB_PAGE_SPEC)` whose `sortMap` allow-lists exactly `{createdAt→created_at}` (`service.ts:7-11`) → unmappable input falls back to the default, never reaches SQL raw. Safe.
- **@crm2/sdk CONTRACT ✓** — `JobView`/`JobType`/`JobStatus`/`JobListQuery`(+`JobResultUrl`) all live in `packages/sdk/src/jobs.ts`, re-exported (`index.ts`), consumed by the API repo/service (`import type … from '@crm2/sdk'`) AND the FE client (`client.ts:581-587` `s.jobs.{list,get}`) — FE invents no shape. `JobView` camelCase (`createdAt`/`startedAt`/`completedAt`) ↔ snake `READ_COLS` reconciled by `db.ts:19 camelize` (verified; test :59-60 asserts `startedAt`/`completedAt` non-null). client.test count 125→127 matches the 2 new client methods.
- **DB ✓ (forward-only, idempotent)** — `BEGIN/COMMIT`; `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS`; CHECKs on type/status/progress; `idx_jobs_owner_recent (created_by, created_at DESC)` exactly serves the tray's `WHERE created_by ORDER BY created_at DESC`. **notifications CHECK widening is SAFE** — `DROP CONSTRAINT IF EXISTS` then `ADD` with a SUPERSET of the prior allowed values (adds `JOB_COMPLETED`/`JOB_FAILED` to type, `DOWNLOAD` to action_type; removes NONE) → no existing row can violate the new CHECK → no migration failure, no data loss. SDK enums (`notifications.ts:17-18,23`) widened in lockstep — contract + DB agree. `created_by … ON DELETE CASCADE` correct (a deleted user's jobs go with them).
- **CODE QUALITY ✓** — no suppressions (grep clean: no `ts-ignore`/`as any`/`eslint-disable`). Business-layer magic numbers named (`clampPct` bounds inline are the 0..100 domain constants, mirrored by the `chk_jobs_progress` CHECK; titles in `DONE_TITLE`/`FAIL_TITLE` `Record<JobType,…>` maps — exhaustive over the union). `error` column stores a **code/message, not a stack** (`index.ts:102`: `AppError.code` ‖ `Error.message` ‖ `'JOB_FAILED'`) — matches mig comment + the `progress=0` reset on fail. Config-gated seam holds: `REDIS_QUEUE_URL` optional in `@crm2/config:12`; `getRealtime()` degrades to `noopRealtime` (so `emit` is safe with no socket server); `setJobNotifier(null)`-tolerant (`notifier?.`). `awaitAllJobs` is a clean test-determinism helper, not prod surface.

### Notifier double-wire / idempotency check (PASS)

`setJobNotifier` (`index.ts:44`) sets a module-global `notifier`; `createApp` calls it on every invocation (`app.ts:64`). **Last-write-wins, idempotent in effect** — each call installs the SAME closure shape over the singleton `notificationService`; multiple `createApp`s (tests) just re-point to an equivalent fn (no accumulation, no listener stacking, unlike `.on()` registration). No double-fire. Same pattern as `setRealtime`/`setPusher`. The only defect on this wire is F1 (the missing `.catch`).

**Bottom line:** ship after F1. The spine is leak-proof, contract-complete, forward-only, and correctly stops at the seam — the worker and processors are genuinely deferred, not half-built.

---

## Audit Panel — B-13 EXPORT-as-job slice (ADR-0030 / ADR-0021) (2026-06-15)

**Slice (UNCOMMITTED working tree, on bf8fdc7 B-7.1 spine):** NEW `platform/export/job.ts` (registry + `exportJobProcessor` + `exportOrEnqueue` + `buildExportFile` + `enqueueExport`), `http/registerJobs.ts` (boot wiring). MODIFIED `modules/jobs/{service,controller,routes}.ts` (presigned `result-url`), `modules/locations/{service,controller}.ts` (`exportAllForJob` + `exportOrEnqueue`), `platform/http.ts` (+`ACCEPTED:202`), `http/app.ts` (`registerJobs()`), `sdk/{client,client.test}.ts` (resultUrl method, count 127→128), `jobs.api.test.ts` (real processor + fake store). `JobResultUrl` type already landed in B-7.1 (forward-prep). Live-verified: 157k export → 202 → job SUCCEEDED → 13MB CSV from MinIO.

**OVERALL VERDICT: FLAG (clear to commit after F1).** Scope is minimal and on-spec; no frozen-standard violation; the 413-catch design is correctness-safe (traced). One real standards deviation — F1, the silent 100k truncation — which violates the "no silent caps" rule and is the one thing that should be addressed (or explicitly DEFERred with a logged carry) before this ships to a user who can request >100k rows. Two INFO notes.

### Findings

- **F1 · MEDIUM (standards) · `modules/locations/service.ts:147-154` (`exportAllForJob`) + `platform/export/job.ts:19` (`MAX_EXPORT_ROWS`)** — **SILENT TRUNCATION confirmed.** `exportAllForJob` issues `repo.list({…, limit: exportJobRowCap()=100_000, offset:0})` and destructures **only `{ items }`**, discarding the `totalCount` the same query returns (`locations/repository.ts:70` returns `{items, totalCount}`). For the prod 157k catalog, `items.length===100_000`, `totalCount===157_000`; `buildExportFile` reports `rowCount: rows.length` = 100_000; the job stores 100k rows and SUCCEEDS. **57k rows vanish with zero signal** — no `capped` flag in the job `result`, no log line naming what was dropped, no error. This is exactly the "no silent caps — log what was dropped" standard being broken, and the live "157k → 13MB CSV" verification almost certainly produced a **truncated** file (157k locations should be ~20MB+ CSV; 13MB is consistent with ~100k rows). Severity MEDIUM not HIGH only because the data is a non-financial reference catalog and the cap is generous — but a user exporting "all" and silently getting 64% is a data-integrity/trust defect. *Disposition (recommend FLAG-now, the cheap surface fix; DEFER-streaming is the proper long fix):* the `totalCount` is already in hand — when `totalCount > rowCount`, EITHER (a) surface a `capped: true, totalCount, rowCount` field in the processor's `result` (and a `logger.warn('export capped', {resource, totalCount, cap})`) so the tray/notification can honestly say "first 100k of 157k", OR (b) treat `totalCount > MAX_EXPORT_ROWS` as a hard `AppError` job-failure ("export exceeds 100k row cap; narrow the filter") rather than a silent partial. Option (a) is the smaller change and keeps the export useful; the streaming-builder follow-up (job.ts:18 comment) then lifts the cap entirely. Do NOT ship a silent partial.

- **F2 · INFO · scope is clean, no speculative code.** Registry + generic `buildExportFile<T>` + per-module `ExportBuild` closure + `exportOrEnqueue` 413-catch + `exportAllForJob` + presigned `result-url` + boot wiring + one real resource (locations) — every piece traces to "an ≥10k `all` export becomes a downloadable job". No second resource pre-wired (tasks/cases correctly NOT registered — they need actor-scope re-resolution, deferred). `MAX_EXPORT_ROWS=100_000` living in `platform/export/job.ts` (not the business/module layer) is **acceptable** — it is a platform-engine guard rail (the export engine's own ceiling), co-located with the processor that enforces it, exposed only via `exportJobRowCap()`; it is not a domain/business constant smuggled into a module. (Contrast: it is genuinely the engine's number, like `EXPORT_JOB_THRESHOLD` which IS env-backed — arguably `MAX_EXPORT_ROWS` should also be env-tunable, but a named platform const is within standard.)

- **F3 · INFO · the `exportOrEnqueue` catch-the-413 design is correctness- and UX-safe.** Traced end-to-end: `exportOrEnqueue` (job.ts:98-115) calls `opts.run(ex)` = `svc.exportData(...)`, and `exportData` runs `repo.list` then `assertExportable(totalCount)` (locations/service.ts:153) — the 413 `EXPORT_TOO_LARGE` is thrown **inside `run`, before any value returns**, so `writeExport` is NEVER reached and `res` is **never touched** (writeExport's only `res.setHeader`/`res.send` calls are its last two lines, after the in-memory body build — index.ts). Therefore at the moment the catch fires, **no headers are sent** and `res.status(202).json(job)` is a clean, valid response. The catch is narrow (`e.code==='EXPORT_TOO_LARGE' && builders.has(resource)`) — any other error, or a resource with no builder, re-throws to `next(e)` → the honest 413 (incremental rollout preserved). No partial-write / double-send risk. UX: the FE gets a `JobView` row to poll, consistent with the spine's tray contract.

### Dimension notes (PASS)

- **@crm2/sdk CONTRACT ✓** — `result-url` returns `JobResultUrl{url,filename}` from `packages/sdk/src/jobs.ts` (committed B-7.1); server `jobService.resultUrl` (service.ts) is typed `Promise<JobResultUrl>`, SDK client `s.jobs.resultUrl(id)` is typed `req<JobResultUrl>` — FE invents no shape. `client.test` count 127→128 matches the one new client method. No new shape coined outside the SDK.
- **RAW SQL ✓** — no SQL added to the slice; `exportAllForJob` goes through `repo.list` (the existing repository), `resultUrl` reads via `jobRepository.getOwned` + `getStorage().signedUrl`. Engine/processor touch no DB directly.
- **SUPPRESSIONS ✓** — grep across all slice files: 0 `as any` / `: any` / `@ts-ignore` / `@ts-expect-error` / `eslint-disable`. The two casts present (`ctx.payload as ExportJobPayload` job.ts:69; `job.result as {storageKey?,filename?}` jobs/service.ts) are unavoidable JSONB-deserialization narrowings of `unknown`, both defensively re-validated (`if (!build)`, `if (!result.storageKey) → JOB_NO_ARTIFACT`).
- **SECURITY / RBAC ✓** — `result-url` is own-job scoped (`getOwned(id, userId)` → null → `notFound()`, IDOR-safe, tested); UUID-shape-guarded `:id` (controller.ts) → bad value clean 404 not pg-22P02-500 (tested for both `/jobs/:id` and `/:id/result-url`); not-ready job → `JOB_NOT_READY` 400 (no presign of an unfinished/foreign artifact); storage key is server-built `exports/${actorId}/${jobId}` (job.ts:75) — actor-namespaced, never client-supplied. Route declared **before** `/:id` with the in-file comment (Express matches in order) — correct, `result-url` can't be swallowed by `/:id`.
- **DB / migrations ✓** — none in this slice (table + CHECK widening landed in B-7.1). Forward-only invariant intact.

**Bottom line:** the engine, the 413-catch, the presigned download, and the scope are all sound and standards-clean. The single thing standing between this and a clean PASS is **F1 — do not ship a silent 100k truncation**; surface a `capped` signal + log (cheap, totalCount already in hand) or fail loudly, then defer the unbounded streaming-builder. Commit after F1.


---

## Audit Panel — B-7 FE background-jobs slice (ADR-0030 / PAGINATION_AND_LOADING_STANDARDS §10-11) (2026-06-15)

**Slice (UNCOMMITTED working tree, on bf8fdc7 spine + d448f97 B-13 BE):** NEW `apps/web/src/components/JobsTray.tsx`, `src/features/jobs/{api.ts,useJobs.ts}`. MODIFIED `packages/sdk/src/export.ts` (`ExportOutcome` union), `src/lib/sdk.ts` (`apiExport` 202-vs-file), `components/ui/data-grid/DataGrid.tsx` (`exportFn→ExportOutcome`; job → toast + `invalidate(['jobs'])`), `components/NotificationBell.tsx` (DOWNLOAD action → `fetchJobResultUrl` → `window.open`), `components/Layout.tsx` (mount `JobsTray` + `useRealtimeJobs`), 13 pages + MasterDataCrud `apiBlob→apiExport`. Live-verified: 157k locations → 202 → toast "Export started in the background" → tray SUCCEEDED + Download + capped warning "100,000 of 157,074 matched rows" → bell incremented via socket.

**OVERALL VERDICT: PASS (clear to commit; 0 must-fix, 2 INFO).** Scope is minimal and exactly on-spec for the B-7 FE slice — every changed line traces to "an enqueued export must be visible, trackable, and downloadable from the shell." No speculative surface. The standards obligations are met in full, and the one thing I gated hardest on — the no-silent-cap rule that I FLAGGED on the BE B-13 slice (F1) — is now honestly surfaced at the UI layer.

### Dimension notes (PASS)
- **SCOPE ✓ — minimal, on-spec.** The slice is the FE consumer of the B-7.1 engine + B-13 export-as-job: a read-only tray (`useJobs`), a socket nudge (`useRealtimeJobs`), one SDK outcome union, one `apiExport` reader, the DataGrid job-branch, the bell DOWNLOAD wire, and the 13-page swap. Nothing builds the producer (already shipped), nothing pre-wires import-job UI (B-14, correctly absent), no FE feature-flag scaffolding invented. The `apiBlob` helper is RETAINED (still the synchronous file path) — not deleted — so non-DataGrid file downloads (UsersPage scope export) keep working untouched.
- **§10-11 COMPLETION DELIVERY ✓ — all three channels present.** §11 mandates bell + toast + in-app. Toast fires on enqueue (DataGrid `runExport` job-branch: "Export started in the background — you can keep working"). In-app tray (`JobsTray`) shows the live row, the active badge, the Download, and the capped warning. Bell delivers completion (`JOB_COMPLETED`/action_type `DOWNLOAD` → clickable Download). "User can keep working" is satisfied — the export is fire-and-forget; no modal blocks the UI.
- **§7/§8 DETERMINATE HEXAGON, REAL % ✓ — no fake progress.** A RUNNING job renders `HexagonLoader percent={running.progress}` (JobsTray:111-116) — the real server-emitted 0..100 from the engine's canonical stage map, NOT an animated guess. `operation={type — N%}`, optional `subStep={stage}`. This is the §7 determinate mode (percent given → outline fills to a real %), §8-compliant. No spinner, no bar, no bouncing dots. The per-row line also shows `{progress}% · {stage}` for non-running actives. Honors the forbidden-loader list.
- **NO-SILENT-CAP HONORED ✓ — the BE F1 fix is now USER-VISIBLE.** I FLAGGED the silent 100k truncation on the B-13 BE slice (F1, MEDIUM). The BE was fixed to emit `result.{capped,totalCount,rowCount}` (verified `platform/export/job.ts:84-93`). This FE slice surfaces it: JobsTray:148-153 renders, when `r.capped`, "{rowCount} of {totalCount} matched rows — refine filters for the full set." in `text-destructive`. The 157k→100k cap is no longer silent at any layer — log (BE) + tray banner (FE). **The trust defect I gated on is closed end-to-end.** Field names match BE emit 1:1 (`capped`/`totalCount`/`rowCount`); a non-capped job sets `totalCount=rowCount` so the banner never spuriously fires.
- **UX-GAP probes — both handled.** (1) **Download fails:** `JobsTray.download` + `NotificationBell.downloadFromNotification` both wrap `fetchJobResultUrl`+`window.open` in try/catch → `toast.error('Could not start the download. Please try again.')`. No silent failure, no dead button. (2) **Job has no result yet:** the Download button only renders for `status==='SUCCEEDED' && type==='EXPORT'` (JobsTray:139); a PENDING/RUNNING job shows progress, a FAILED job shows its error (`j.error ?? 'Failed'`, destructive). No premature presign of an unfinished artifact (BE also 400s `JOB_NOT_READY`). A SUCCEEDED job with a missing `result.filename` degrades to "Download file" (sane default).

### INFO (not findings)
- **INFO-1 · empty-state + a11y are present, not gold-plated.** Empty tray → "No background jobs"; button `aria-label` reflects active count + `aria-expanded`; outside-click + Escape close the popover. Matches the NotificationBell precedent. No over-engineering.
- **INFO-2 · the capped banner copy is honest and actionable** ("refine filters for the full set") rather than a bare number — good operator UX. The 100k cap itself remains a platform const (BE NOTE, carried); the streaming-builder follow-up lifts it. Not an FE concern.

**Bottom line:** ships. Minimal, on-spec, all three §11 channels, determinate real-% Hexagon, and — the bit I cared about most — the silent-cap defect I flagged on the backend is now truthfully shown to the user. No must-fix.

## 2026-06-15 — B-7.2 worker tier (Valkey + BullMQ out-of-process worker + 200k cap) — VERDICT: PASS

Adversarial audit of the uncommitted B-7.2 slice (`git diff`): `platform/jobs/index.ts`, `main.ts` (ROLE=worker), `registerJobs.ts`, `app.ts`, `platform/export/job.ts` + `packages/config` (cap), `docker-compose.yml` (valkey :6380), `ALLOWED_DEPENDENCIES` (+bullmq), `ADR-0030`, `.env.example`.

### Findings

- **SCOPE ✓ minimal/on-spec.** The slice is exactly the worker tier: lazy BullMQ `Queue` (enqueue) + `Worker` (consume), a `ROLE=worker` boot in `main.ts`, and `registerJobs()` refactored out of `createApp` so both the api and the worker run the SAME registrations (no duplicated wiring). No streaming builders, no DB cursor, no IMPORT path — correctly DEFERRED (carried in ADR + `EXPORT_JOB_MAX_ROWS` comment). No speculative infra; `report` role still warns "not yet implemented". Every changed line traces to the worker path or the cap.
- **STANDARDS ✓.** `bullmq` added to ALLOWED_DEPENDENCIES with rationale + the gate it's config-gated on (`REDIS_QUEUE_URL`) under ADR-0030; the ADR has a dated "Worker tier — BUILT (2026-06-15)" section. No new architecture without an ADR. The config-gated seam mirrors realtime/storage exactly: `getQueue()` returns `null` when `REDIS_QUEUE_URL` unset (in-process), resolves a lazy-imported `Queue` when set — identical pattern to the socket.io adapter's `REDIS_CACHE_URL` gate. The cap is config (`EXPORT_JOB_MAX_ROWS`, zod-validated, default 200000); the only literals in the platform layer (`JOB_QUEUE='acs-jobs'`, `concurrency:4`, `removeOnFail:500`) are infra constants, not business magic — acceptable.
- **F1 (prior ledger) RESOLVED ✓.** The MEDIUM silent-truncation defect I flagged on B-7.x is now fixed AND verified by raising the cap: builder returns `totalCount`; processor computes `capped = matched > rowCount`, `logger.warn('export capped…')`, and surfaces `{capped, totalCount}` in the job result (`export/job.ts:80-90`). `exportAllForJob` now fetches `limit: exportJobRowCap()` and returns the full `totalCount` (`locations/service.ts:167-178`). With the cap at 200k the 157k catalog returns `capped:false` / 157,074 rows — the export is now COMPLETE and HONEST. The thing I most cared about is closed.
- **F2 · LOW (perf, carried — NOT a block) · `platform/export/job.ts` (200k cap, no streaming).** Raising 100k→200k without streaming widens the worker-OOM window for **XLSX** specifically: `exceljs` holds the whole workbook object graph in memory (~hundreds of bytes/cell × N cols × 200k rows = potentially >1GB for a wide sheet), whereas CSV is near-linear string concatenation. The live verification was **CSV** (157k), so the XLSX-at-200k case is UNTESTED. Judgement: 200k is a safe default *for the real data* (157k catalog is the largest live set, and it's CSV-dominant), and the cap is honest (`capped` above it), so this is not a ship-blocker. But the cap is format-blind — a future caller exporting 200k rows as XLSX on a memory-constrained worker could OOM. The streaming-builder + DB-cursor follow-up (already carried in ADR + config comment) is the correct fix; until then the ADR/`.env.example` note "raise only with streaming builders" should also caution that **XLSX may warrant a lower effective cap than CSV**. FLAG-for-the-carry, not for this slice.
- **DEV-FRICTION ✓.** Dev defaults to in-process (env unset → no Valkey, no worker) — correct: tests/dev pull nothing (lazy import), the contract is still exercised in-process. The "to test the queue path you must run BOTH `docker compose up valkey` AND a `ROLE=worker` process" is documented in `.env.example` (the new block spells out both URLs + the worker command) AND in the ADR's BUILT section. No hidden setup.
- **NO SUPPRESSIONS / NO RAW SQL in slice.** Two `as` casts (`bullJob.data as {…}`, `ctx.payload as ExportJobPayload`) are unavoidable JSONB/queue-deserialization narrowings of `unknown`, both defensively guarded downstream (`if (!build)`).

**Bottom line:** PASS — ships. Minimal, on-spec, ADR + ALLOWED_DEPENDENCIES honored, seam mirrors realtime/storage, and the silent-cap defect is provably closed by the raised+honest cap. One non-blocking carry: the 200k cap is format-blind; XLSX-at-cap is untested and is the real OOM risk — fold an XLSX caution into the streaming-builder follow-up.

---

## 2026-06-15 — B-14 background large-import tier (IMPORT job; `platform/import/{index,format}.ts`, `platform/storage/index.ts` +get, `packages/config` IMPORT_JOB_MAX_ROWS 200k, `modules/locations/{service,controller}`, `http/registerJobs.ts`, web `ImportModal.tsx`/`JobsTray.tsx`, sdk test + 4 storage fakes; working tree, uncommitted) — VERDICT: **PASS** (no BLOCK/must-fix; 1 FLAG-minor-carry, 2 INFO)

Adversarial read of the full `git diff` + independent re-verify: `pnpm -w typecheck` 8/8 FULL TURBO; `pnpm -w run boundaries` **0 errors** (14 pre-existing orphan warnings, all e2e/config). The slice is the import mirror of the B-7/B-13/B-7.2 export-job tier I already cleared: a registry-backed `ImportRunner`, an `importJobProcessor`, an `importConfirmOrEnqueue` sync-vs-job decision, a `storage.get` round-trip, and the FE 202 handling. Live context confirmed (10,001-row pincode CSV → 202 → SUCCEEDED 10001/10001 → import_log + "Import complete" bell + tray "IMPORTED 10,001 OF 10,001 ROWS"; <10k still inline).

### Adversarial findings (the four CEO probes)

1. **SCOPE ✓ — minimal, on-spec, mirrors export 1:1.** Every changed line traces to "an import ≥10k must become a trackable background job instead of an honest 413." The pattern is the export tier's twin: `registerImportRunner`/`importRunners` map == `registerExportBuilder`/`builders`; `importJobProcessor` == `exportJobProcessor`; `importConfirmOrEnqueue` == `exportOrEnqueue`; `imports/${userId}/${uuid}.bin` key namespace == `exports/${actorId}/...`; 202+JobView on enqueue == export. No speculative surface — no per-row error-file plumbing, no FE flag scaffolding, no import-progress granularity invented. **Incremental rollout is correct AND honest:** ONLY `locations` registers a runner; the other 9 import modules pass no `maxRows`, so `assertImportable` defaults to the sync threshold and they keep their unchanged ≥10k 413 ("split the file"). That asymmetry is documented in the `assertImportable` doc-comment, the service comment, and ADR-0030 framing — a caller is never silently degraded. Acceptable.
2. **FROZEN STANDARDS ✓.** The `@crm2/sdk` contract is reused, not invented — the IMPORT job `result` is plain counts (`totalRows/successRows/failedRows/durationMs`), a subset of `ImportConfirmResult`, surfaced through the existing `JobView.result: Record<string,unknown>` channel; the FE reads it via the same optional-narrowed `jobResult()` shape. `JOB_COMPLETED`/`JOB_FAILED` + `DOWNLOAD` action-type test assertion is a real-enum fix, not a new shape. Thresholds are config (`IMPORT_JOB_THRESHOLD` 10k, `IMPORT_JOB_MAX_ROWS` 200k, both zod `coerce.int.positive`); the only literals in the platform layer are the `imports/` key prefix and `.bin` ext (infra constants, not business magic) — same latitude I granted the export `exports/` prefix. No suppressions, no `any`, raw SQL stays in repos (import writes go through `locationService.create`, which is audited). Clean.
3. **DROPPED PER-ROW ERROR FILE for background imports — ACCEPTABLE GAP, not a flag (disposition: CARRY as a named follow-up).** Sync imports return `errors[]` → the modal renders the downloadable error CSV; the background path deliberately drops `errors[]` from the job result (the code comment is explicit: "the per-row error file is a later enhancement"). I probed whether this is a trust defect like the silent-cap I BLOCKED on B-13 — it is NOT, because nothing is *silently* lost: (a) the per-row failures are durably written to `import_log` (the comment's claim, consistent with the existing import audit path), (b) the job result's `failedRows` count is surfaced in the tray ("· N failed"), so the operator is TRUTHFULLY told some rows failed and how many. The difference from the silent-cap is exactly the trust line: a count + a durable log is honest disclosure; a missing 57k with no flag was not. The gap is "the operator can't one-click the failing-rows CSV for a background import — they must read import_log." For a 10k–200k bulk catalog load that's a degraded-but-honest UX, not a correctness or trust defect. **Disposition: ACCEPT for this slice; carry "surface the background-import error file (store errors[] alongside the file, expose via a job artifact like the export download)" as the named B-14 follow-up** — symmetric with how the export streaming-builder was carried.
4. **61s/no-granular-progress for 10k — ACCEPTABLE, not a flag.** The processor emits real (not fake) progress at 15/40/95 with honest stage labels ("Fetching file"/"Importing rows"/"Finishing") — it is NOT a fabricated bar, so the §7/§8 no-fake-progress rule is honored; it is merely *coarse* (the row loop between 40 and 95 has no per-batch tick, so a 10k import sits at 40% for ~61s). This is the same coarseness the export processor ships with and which the B-7.2 worker tier exists to make non-blocking for prod — the work is off the request thread, the user is explicitly told "keep working, we'll notify you," and the bell + tray deliver completion. Coarse honest progress on a backgrounded job is acceptable; per-batch progress is a nicety, not a §11 obligation. **INFO-carry, not a flag.**

### INFO (not findings)
- **INFO-1 · the count-then-route decision is conservative (safe direction).** `countImportRows` counts the raw grid (header-excluded) BEFORE blank-row filtering, while the actual processed `rows.length` filters blanks (`mapRows` `anyValue` skip). So `count ≥ actual` always — a file near the boundary can only *over*-route to async, never *under*-route a true-≥10k file into the inline path. Erring toward the background tier is the safe error. (Principal covers the correctness mechanics.)
- **INFO-2 · FE closes the modal + fires a toast on 202, no blocking modal.** §11 completion channels are all present (toast on enqueue, tray live row + final "Imported N of M", bell on done). "User can keep working" satisfied. Consistent with the export FE slice I cleared.

**Bottom line:** ships. Minimal, on-spec, a faithful mirror of the export tier whose standards I already validated; the incremental single-resource rollout is honest and documented; thresholds are config; and the one thing I gate hardest on — silent data loss — does NOT recur here: failed rows are counted in the tray AND logged to import_log, so the dropped error-file is a degraded-but-honest UX gap, correctly carried as the named follow-up, not a trust defect. No must-fix.

---

## 2026-06-15 — B-5 Saved Views (per-user named DataGrid views; DATAGRID_STANDARD §10) — VERDICT: PASS

Adversarial audit of the UNCOMMITTED slice. NEW: `db/v2/migrations/0051_saved_views.sql`, `apps/api/src/modules/saved-views/{repository,service,controller,routes}.ts` + `__tests__/saved-views.api.test.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/ui/data-grid/SavedViewsPicker.tsx`, `packages/sdk/src/savedViews.ts` + test. MODIFIED: `http/app.ts`, `data-grid/DataGrid.tsx`, `packages/sdk/src/{client,client.test,index}.ts`. Gate green (verify EXIT=0, SDK 102, API 7).

**OVERALL: PASS — clear to commit. 0 BLOCK, 0 must-fix, 3 FLAG-minor (UX/polish, all carry-or-fix-inline), 2 INFO.**

### Standards gate (the bit I gate hardest on) — all honored
- **No suppressions** in any new file (grep eslint-disable/@ts-*/`as any`/`: any` → none). **No hardcoded colors** in `SavedViewsPicker.tsx` (no hex/rgb/hsl; tokens only — `border-border`, `bg-card`, `text-muted-foreground`, `text-primary`, `text-destructive`, `hover:bg-row-hover`). **UPPERCASE display** honored via global CSS — NO `.toUpperCase()` in the component; view names are stored verbatim (case-sensitive user input, `name varchar(120)`, no write-side UPPER) and uppercased only on screen by the global `body{text-transform}` — exactly ENGINEERING_STANDARDS §7 / UPPERCASE_DISPLAY_STANDARD.
- **@crm2/sdk contract present per endpoint:** all 5 endpoints have typed `sdk.savedViews.{list,create,update,remove,setDefault}` (`client.ts:592-602`) + transport test asserting count 133 and the `?resourceKey=cases` URL (`client.test.ts:322-330`). Note the WEB app consumes via its local `api<T>()` wrapper with hand-written paths (`SavedViewsPicker.tsx:27,62,77,85,89`), NOT `sdk.savedViews.*` — this is the EXISTING house pattern (JobsTray/NotificationBell do identical raw `api()` calls); the SDK layer still carries the canonical contract. Not a deviation introduced here.
- **DataGrid/pagination standard:** picker mounts once in the shared toolbar via `resourceKey={queryKey}` (`DataGrid.tsx:435`) — zero per-page edits, on-spec. `queryKey` values verified UNIQUE per grid (cases/rates/locations/dedupe/client-products/verification-units + consts/`config.queryKey`) → no resourceKey collision. `captureState()` correctly excludes `page` only (a view is a query, not a scroll pos); `applyState` filters `if(v)` — consistent with DataGrid's own `if(v)` filter read (empty values are meaningless both ways → no data loss).

### Scope (Karpathy) — minimal, on-spec
Every changed line traces to "per-user named grid-state snapshots." Own-user scope is identity not permission (no permission gate on routes — correct, mirrors notifications/jobs; `requireUserId` 401s, `:id` not-owned → 404 IDOR-safe). Migration is forward-only/idempotent (`IF NOT EXISTS`, partial-unique default index in DB not just service). Set-default clears the sibling in the SAME tx (`repository.ts:42-48,110-131`) so the partial index never rejects. No speculative surface (no sharing, no cross-user read, no export of views, no FE flag infra invented).

### FLAG (minor — UX/polish; none block)
1. **F1 · LOW · `SavedViewsPicker.tsx:83-91` — silent failure on toggle/update/delete.** `setDefaultMut`, `updateMut`, `removeMut` have NO `onError` (only `createMut` does, at :69). A failed set-default / "update to current filters" / delete shows the user nothing — the row just doesn't change. Not a trust/data defect (server is authoritative; `invalidate()` on success re-syncs truth), but it's an honest-feedback gap vs. the create path and the JobsTray/bell precedent (which `toast.error` on every failed mutation). **Disposition: SHOULD-FIX inline — add a `toast.error('Could not update the view.')` (or similar) to the three mutations before commit; one line each.**
2. **F2 · LOW · `SavedViewsPicker.tsx:170` — destructive delete has no confirm.** `×` deletes immediately on click (`removeMut.mutate(v.id)`), no confirm + no undo. A saved view is cheap to recreate and the icon is small/distinct, so this is acceptable-by-judgement, but it's a one-click destructive action on named user data. **Disposition: ACCEPT for this slice (low blast radius); CARRY as a nicety (confirm-on-delete or toast-with-undo) if the picker grows.**
3. **F3 · INFO→LOW · `SavedViewsPicker.tsx:51-58` — default auto-applies once-per-mount, deps include recreated `applyState`.** The `appliedDefault` ref + `viewsQuery.isLoading` guard make this correct (verified: re-runs are short-circuited; bookmarked/filtered URLs are respected via the `hasState` check). The `applyState`/`params` in deps are lint-satisfying but inert given the ref-guard. No bug; noting because "auto-apply on clean open" is the one behavior most likely to surprise (e.g. a default view silently rewrites the URL on every fresh navigation to the list — intended per spec, but worth a product-confirm that operators want default-on-open vs. opt-in).

### INFO
- **INFO-1 · 409 mapping is clean.** Duplicate (user,resource,name) → `23505` → `SAVED_VIEW_NAME_EXISTS` 409, surfaced by the picker as a field error (:71-74). update() also maps it (`repository.ts:92`). Tested both create + cross-grid/cross-user allow (api test :65-88).
- **INFO-2 · test coverage is genuinely adversarial** (DB-gated): 401-unauth, 400-no-resourceKey, per-user isolation, 409 dupe + cross-grid/cross-user allow, rename+recapture, IDOR 404 (non-owner PUT/DELETE/set-default), bad-uuid→404-not-500, empty-update→400, single-default invariant incl. clear. Strong.

**Bottom line:** ships. The frozen-standards gate I own is clean end-to-end — no suppressions, no hardcoded colors, CSS-only uppercase, SDK contract per endpoint, single shared-toolbar mount with unique resourceKeys, own-user scope that's IDOR-safe and DB-enforced. The only thing between this and a spotless PASS is F1 (add `onError` toasts to the three silent mutations — one line each, inline before commit). F2/F3 are carries/product-confirms, not blockers.

## 2026-06-15 — B-11/B-12 OpenAPI surface + SDK-drift gate (ADR-0031, validate-don't-replace) — VERDICT: PASS

Last item of the 6-item platform cluster. Audited adversarially: ran the gate fresh, tampered the spec to prove the gate bites, audited deps/suppressions/scope, and stress-tested the "honest about phase-1 vs phase-2" claim. **Ships.**

### Standards gate (the bit I gate hardest on) — all honored
- **No new dependency.** `document.ts`/`cli.ts`/`contract.test.ts` import only `express` (already ALLOWED_DEPENDENCIES.md:8), node builtins (`fs`/`url`), workspace `@crm2/logger`, and `vitest`. **No `@asteasolutions/zod-to-openapi`** — correctly deferred to phase 2 (added "when it earns its place"). `tsx` (cli runner) already a devDep (`apps/api/package.json:43`). Route walk is hand-rolled regexp-on-mount → zero-dep as the ADR claims.
- **No suppressions.** `grep -rE 'eslint-disable|@ts-(ignore|expect-error|nocheck)|istanbul ignore'` over the new dir = 0. The Express-4 router internals are reached via a structurally-typed `unknown` cast (`document.ts:23-31,56-58`), not `any` (banned) — clean.
- **Governance complete (ADR + registry + CI gate, all three present and coherent):** ADR-0031 exists, Status Accepted, lays out the rejected "generate the SDK" path honestly. `COMPLIANCE_GAPS_REGISTRY.md` B-11→✅ FIXED (phase 1), B-12→✅ FIXED, **both with accurate caveats** (B-11 "schema bodies deferred"; B-12 "response-shape drift caught in phase 2; request drift already prevented by shared zod" — verified true: SDK input types are `z.infer` of shared `Create*Schema`). CI step 7+8 rewritten from the dead `sdk:gen` stub to a real `pnpm openapi` + `git diff --exit-code apps/api/openapi.json` gate (`.github/workflows/ci.yml:97-106`).

### Adversarial verification (I did not trust the green check)
- **Drift gate actually bites:** injected a phantom `/api/v2/__tamper__` path into committed `openapi.json` → contract test #1 (`contract.test.ts:33`) FAILS as designed; restored → clean. Re-emitting via `pnpm openapi` then `git diff --exit-code` = EXIT 0 (deterministic `JSON.stringify`, prettier-ignored at `.prettierignore:8-9` so format never fights the diff).
- **SDK-parity is non-vacuous:** the test extracts **133** `/api/v2/...` references from `packages/sdk/src/client.ts` (matches the ADR's "~133 typed methods") + `reqBlob`→`/export` synthesis, asserts every one resolves to a real mounted route. Not an empty set silently passing.
- **Spec coheres with the live app:** 180 paths / 201 operations; `openapi: 3.1.0`; the 4 PUBLIC_PATHS (`/health`,`/time`,`/auth/login`,`/auth/refresh`) emit `security:[]` and **only** those 4 — cross-checked against `app.ts:75-77` mount order (global `authenticate()` is token-optional; real enforcement is per-route `requirePermission`, so "public = no permission guard" is the correct phase-1 reading). No phantom routes.
- **DB-free as claimed:** `env -u DATABASE_URL pnpm openapi` = EXIT 0. Generation never touches the pool. Contract test runs in the **normal** suite (`vitest.config.ts include: src/**/*.test.ts` matches `__tests__/contract.test.ts`), not CI-only — gate can't be skipped locally.
- **Self-inflicted false alarm, ruled out:** my first `pnpm --filter … exec vitest run` showed 11 failures across password/totp/storage/push/system + the contract test — ALL `DATABASE_URL: Invalid input`, i.e. my invocation didn't load `apps/api/.env` the way `pnpm test`/`pnpm verify` does. Re-ran with env sourced → contract test 3/3 PASS. **Not a regression in this change**; the owner's `pnpm verify` EXIT=0 stands.

### Scope (Karpathy) — minimal, on-spec
205 LOC across 3 source files + a 180-path generated artifact + 5 small config/doc edits. Every line traces to "emit an OpenAPI surface from the live app and gate drift." No speculative schema infra, no FE flag, no SDK rewrite — exactly the validate-don't-replace boundary the CTO chose. The work is **honest about done-vs-deferred**: phase-1 surface is shipped and the deferral of request/response schema bodies is stated in the ADR Consequences, the registry caveats, the `info.description`, AND each operation's `responses.default.description`. B-11 AND B-12 are both genuinely delivered (not one punted under cover of the other) — B-11 = the committed spec + `pnpm openapi`; B-12 = the two-mechanism drift gate. No overclaim.

### FLAG (minor — doc hygiene; does not block)
1. **F1 · LOW · `docs/CI_CD_STANDARDS.md:13,37` — Part 21 still describes the rejected `sdk:gen` mechanism.** Lines 13 and 37 say the gate is `pnpm sdk:gen + git diff` / `sdk:gen + git diff + contract:web/contract:mobile`, but ADR-0031 rejected SDK generation in favor of `pnpm openapi` + openapi.json diff. The standards doc now lags the ADR + the actual CI step. Not a code defect and the CI file itself is correct, but the "source of truth" standard text is stale. **Disposition: SHOULD-FIX — update Part 21 rows to reference `pnpm openapi`/openapi.json drift (and note SDK→route parity lives in the contract test), so the standard matches the activated implementation. One-doc edit; out of scope to fix here per no-modify-code, flagged for the owner.**

### INFO
- **INFO-1 · The "schemas = phase 2" gap is a real but disclosed limitation, not a hidden one.** Response-shape drift is NOT caught today; the ADR/registry/spec all say so. This is the honest phase boundary, not an overclaim — the validate gate delivers exactly the surface-drift + SDK-deadlink safety it promises, no more.
- **INFO-2 · Generated artifact is prettier-ignored AND deterministically ordered** (`document.ts:72-73` sort by path then method) → stable git-diff, no spurious churn. Good future-proofing for the gate's signal-to-noise.

---

## 2026-06-15 — Lifecycle redesign DESIGN REVIEW (ADR-0032 PROPOSED; `docs/specs/2026-06-15-lifecycle-design/2026-06-15-v2-lifecycle-redesign.md`) — VERDICT: **FLAG** (design-only; do not commit migrations/endpoints until F1+F2 resolved)

Adversarial review of the PROPOSED two-track lifecycle against the owner's four 2026-06-15 decisions and the gap map (`06-cross-system-gap-map.md`). The decisions are faithfully encoded at the *structural* level (single-layer result §4, case-level outcome §4, two-track completion §1-3, native `/api/v2` + device rebase §5/§10.6). The two-track model itself is sound and device-safe. But there are two genuine business-rule holes the design does not close, and several smaller gaps. **Design-only — nothing built — so this is a FLAG to fix the spec before build slices 1-2, not a BLOCK on code.**

### Findings

- **F1 · HIGH (product correctness) · §2 (auto-complete) vs §3 (`case.finalize` "commission settle for all task legs") vs §10 slice 5 ("gate = task COMPLETED & !REVOKED") — COMMISSION TIMING IS CONTRADICTORY/UNDERSPECIFIED.** Three sections disagree on *when the field agent earns commission*. D2 makes the TASK terminal on field submit (no review gate) and §10.5 states the commission gate is `task.status=COMPLETED & !REVOKED` (task-based, per the protected invariant "commission/billing are task-based"). But §3 settles commission at **case.finalize** (AWAITING_COMPLETION→COMPLETED, office-driven). Those are different moments: a multi-leg case can sit in AWAITING_COMPLETION for days while the office decides the case result. If commission is gated on task-COMPLETED it is earned at submit (D2's whole point — no waiting); if it settles at case-finalize the field agent IS waiting on the office, which silently re-introduces the very office-gate D2 removed. **This is the keystone the gap map (§5) flagged (v1 deferred commission to finalize only when the review flag was ON — and we removed that gate).** MUST resolve in the spec: state explicitly that commission accrues at TASK COMPLETED (independent of case-finalize) and that §3's "settle for all task legs" is a no-op/idempotent reconcile, OR that it genuinely defers to finalize (and then own the consequence: D2 did not actually free the agent from the office). Cannot be left ambiguous into slice 1/5.

- **F2 · HIGH (product correctness, the charter's explicit probe) · §3/§4 — ONE CASE-LEVEL RESULT FOR A MULTI-TASK CASE IS OPERATIONALLY UNDER-SPECIFIED WHEN LEGS DISAGREE.** D3 collapses the official result to a single `cases.verification_outcome`. For a single-task case this is strictly better (kills v1's VT-000199 fragmentation). But the design never says what the office records when a case has **multiple tasks whose verdicts differ** — e.g. a Residence verification = POSITIVE and an Office verification = NEGATIVE on the same case, or a field task POSITIVE + a KYC/desk leg REFER. v1 carried a per-task outcome precisely so multi-leg cases could report each leg; D3 demotes `case_tasks.verification_outcome` to a non-printed note (§4). So the client report (§4: "prints `cases.verification_outcome`") shows ONE verdict for a case that did two different verifications — and the per-leg detail is explicitly *never printed*. Two real questions the spec must answer: (a) **what is the case result when legs disagree** — worst-of ladder (FRAUD>NEGATIVE>REFER>POSITIVE)? office free-choice? — and (b) **does the bank actually order multi-verification cases**, and if so does it expect a per-verification verdict on the report (Zion prints per-document)? If yes, a single case-level outcome is a *regression* in reporting fidelity, and the demoted per-task column should stay printable. **This is the single biggest product risk in the redesign and it is unaddressed.** MUST: spec the multi-leg result rule + confirm with owner whether per-leg verdicts must appear on the client report. (Mixed field+KYC case is the same problem — KYC leg + field leg, one outcome.)

- **F3 · MEDIUM (correctness/state-machine) · §3 rollup vs `case.finalize` — AWAITING_COMPLETION CAN SILENTLY REVERT OUT FROM UNDER A FINALIZING OFFICER (TOCTOU).** §3: rollup moves IN_PROGRESS↔AWAITING_COMPLETION automatically; `AWAITING_COMPLETION→IN_PROGRESS` fires when "a new task added / revisit created." So: office opens the finalize screen on an AWAITING_COMPLETION case → a revisit/new task is created concurrently (or a completed task is revoked, §2 row "COMPLETED→REVOKED…rollup recheck") → rollup drops the case back to IN_PROGRESS → the officer's `case.finalize` POST must now be rejected. The design says case writers use OCC `version` (good) but `case.finalize` is only listed as a transition *from* AWAITING_COMPLETION — it must explicitly **409 INVALID_TRANSITION if the case is no longer AWAITING_COMPLETION at write time**, and the spec should say the officer is re-queued. Also: §2 allows COMPLETED→REVOKED on a task "if was COMPLETED, requires reason (rare)" with "rollup recheck" — but once the CASE is COMPLETED with a recorded result, can a task still be revoked underneath it? That reopens a closed, reported case. Spec must state whether task-revoke is blocked once `case.status=COMPLETED`.

- **F4 · MEDIUM (scope/invariant) · §6 — DEMOTING (NOT DROPPING) `case_tasks.verification_outcome` LEAVES A DUAL-WRITE RESULT SURFACE, the exact shape of v1's bug.** §4/§6 keep `case_tasks.verification_outcome` "as an optional per-task office note … never printed." v1's VT-000199 fragmentation was caused by *multiple result columns existing and the report reading the wrong one*. Keeping a demoted-but-writable per-task outcome alongside the new authoritative `cases.verification_outcome` recreates that exact two-column hazard — a future reader/report can grab the wrong one. If F2 concludes per-leg verdicts are NOT needed, the column should be **dropped**, not demoted (the design even offers this, §6 "OR drop in a later migration"). Pick one in the spec; "keep it as a note" is how the v1 bug was born. (If F2 concludes per-leg IS needed, then it is not a "note" — it is authoritative-per-leg and must be printed, which contradicts §4.)

- **F5 · LOW (ops/edge) · §3 — `AWAITING_COMPLETION` queue has no SLA / no "stuck case" surfacing, and there is no path for the office to send a case BACK for rework without a full revisit.** The office sees "case ready" but if the evidence is inadequate the only modeled action is revisit/recheck = a NEW billable task. There is no lightweight "return to field for a fix" — every correction costs a commissionable task. That may be intended (clean billing/audit, gap map §4 device-safety) but the spec should state it explicitly as a product decision, because operators will ask for it. Also no mention of who watches AWAITING_COMPLETION aging (a case can park there forever; nothing auto-completes — §3). FLAG-for-the-carry.

- **F6 · LOW (contract) · §5 — the sync delta arrays (`revokedAssignmentIds`, `deletedTaskIds`) are named as "currently hard-coded empty" and now to be populated, but the design does not state the REVOKED-task propagation path to the device.** Mobile break-risk register (gap map §6.1/§6.2): a task REVOKED on web after the device already started/completed it must reach the device via the delta so it doesn't silently keep or re-submit. §2 lists "revokedAssignmentIds delta" for REVOKE but §5 only says "populate the delta arrays" without specifying the COMPLETED-then-REVOKED-on-web case reaches the device. Confirm in slice 2 spec.

### Confirmations (PASS dimensions)
- **Owner decisions faithfully encoded (structure):** D1 single-layer (§4, no `task_backend_reviews`), D2 two-track (§1-3, field submit auto-completes task), D3 case-level outcome (§4 `cases.verification_outcome` authoritative + printed), D4 native `/api/v2` + device rebase (§5 path move only, §10.6). ✓
- **Device-safety invariant HONORED:** "rework = always a NEW task, never re-open a delivered task" (§1, §7 hard rule) — directly answers gap-map §6.2 silent-work-loss landmine. ✓ Strongest part of the design.
- **Locked mobile contract respected at the shape level:** Idempotency-Key on writes, 409=success on start/complete/revoke (NOT form-submit/priority), UUID `:id`, EXIF-strip/watermark (§5). ✓ (API/Contract auditor owns the byte-level proof.)
- **VT-000199 fragmentation root-caused and (single-task) fixed:** report prints the office decision by construction (§4). ✓ — modulo F2/F4 (multi-leg + demoted column reintroduce the hazard).
- **OCC + scope/IDOR guards carried** (§2 guards: 404 scope, 409 STALE/INVALID_TRANSITION, version bump on every status writer). ✓
- **Scope discipline (design-level):** the doc adds only the missing spine (rollup service, ingest endpoints, case-finalize, lineage cols) — no speculative engine, KYC stays a unit subtype, commission deferred to a later engine. ✓

### OPEN items carried forward
- F1 commission-timing contradiction → resolve in spec BEFORE slice 1/5 (keystone).
- F2 multi-leg / mixed field+KYC single-result rule + owner confirm on per-leg report fidelity → BEFORE slice 1/4.
- F3 finalize TOCTOU 409 + can-a-task-be-revoked-under-a-COMPLETED-case → spec the transition guards.
- F4 drop-vs-demote `case_tasks.verification_outcome` decision (tie to F2 outcome).
- F5 AWAITING_COMPLETION aging/SLA + explicit "no lightweight return-to-field, every fix is a billable task" product decision.
- F6 REVOKED (incl. COMPLETED-then-REVOKED) propagation to device via delta — pin in slice 2 spec.
- Carry from prior ledger still live: index every default-sort/sortable column before cases/locations slices (RATCHET); B-22 dropdown limit=200.

**Bottom line:** PASS. The cluster-tail lands clean — zero new deps, zero suppressions, full ADR+registry+CI governance, a drift gate I personally proved bites, and an unusually honest done-vs-deferred story for a "phase 1." The only open item is doc-hygiene F1 (CI_CD_STANDARDS Part 21 text still names the rejected `sdk:gen`); fix the standard text to match the shipped gate.

---

## 2026-06-15 — slice-1 commit review (ADR-0032 case lifecycle spine; `db/v2/migrations/0052_case_lifecycle.sql`, cases module repo/service/controller/routes + test, `packages/access` perms, `packages/sdk` cases/client, web `CaseDetailPage.tsx`, openapi.json; working tree) — VERDICT: **PASS** (0 BLOCK, 0 must-fix, 1 FLAG-minor, 2 INFO)

Adversarial per-commit read of the full `git diff` + 0052 migration against the owner's four decisions and my own prior design-review OPEN items (F1–F6). The slice faithfully implements the two-track spine and — crucially — honors the very resolutions I owner-resolved at design time. **Ships.**

### Owner-decision fidelity (the lens) — all honored
- **D1 single-layer (field records nothing):** no field-assessment column, no `task_backend_reviews`. The only field columns added are `case_tasks.started_at` + `form_data` (evidence, written by slice-2 ingest) — additive read-model stability, declared in spec §6 as part of 0052, NOT a result surface. ✓
- **D2 two-track:** task completion is field/desk-driven (`/complete` → COMPLETED, no review gate); CASE completion is office-driven via the new `POST /:id/finalize`. Rollup parks the case in AWAITING_COMPLETION; only `case.finalize` ever sets COMPLETED (`repository.ts` recompute comment + UPDATE never emits COMPLETED). ✓
- **D3 per-task office result KEPT + ONE final case verdict, distinct:** migration explicitly does NOT touch/demote `case_tasks.verification_outcome` (0041) — comment lines 21-22. New `cases.verification_outcome` is net-new, office-authored at finalize. The flagship test (`cases.api.test.ts:80-106`) records per-task POSITIVE then case-verdict **NEGATIVE** and asserts BOTH survive on the read model (`tasks[0].verificationOutcome === 'POSITIVE'` AND case `verificationOutcome === 'NEGATIVE'`) — the two-track distinction is asserted, not assumed. This directly discharges my design F2/F4. ✓

### CEO F1 commission-timing resolution — HONORED (deferred, not mis-placed)
`git diff | grep -iE 'commission|billing|payout|accrue'` = **empty**. Commission is NOT wired in slice 1 — exactly the slice-5 plan, and `finalizeCase` does no settlement. The F1 keystone risk (silently settling commission at case-finalize and re-introducing the office gate D2 removed) does **not** materialize: finalize only writes the verdict + closes. Clean deferral. ✓

### Scope creep — none
No slice-2 ingest snuck in: grep for `/start`, `/verification/`, `/attachments`, `sync/download`, `/priority`, `/revoke` route additions = empty. The only new route is `/:id/finalize`. `started_at`/`form_data` are the sole forward-looking columns and are spec-sanctioned for 0052. Every changed line traces to "case rollup + finalize + verdict UI." ✓

### Security / correctness (the bits I gate hardest on)
- **Case-grain scope on finalize (Security's slice-1 blocker) — present.** `service.finalizeCase` calls `resolveScope(actor)` → `repo.caseFinalizeState(caseId, scope)` which composes `caseScopePredicate` (`repository.ts:167`); out-of-scope → null → 404 IDOR-safe. The route carries only `authorize(CASE_FINALIZE)` (no record-access mw) — correct: scope is enforced in-service at case grain, NOT the task-assignee middleware. Test `:130-138` asserts out-of-scope BACKEND_USER → 404. ✓
- **OCC + transition guards — real.** `finalizeCase` UPDATE is `WHERE version=$5 AND status='AWAITING_COMPLETION'`; on 0-row it re-reads to disambiguate NOT_FOUND / INVALID_TRANSITION / stale. Service pre-checks status (409) and version travels outside the schema via `requireVersion`. Test `:108-156` asserts not-AWAITING→409, verifier→403, out-of-scope→404, stale→409, double-finalize→409. Genuinely adversarial. ✓
- **Rollup single-writer + anti-staleness — implemented as designed.** `recomputeCaseStatus` (`repository.ts:264`) is the single case-status writer, `SELECT … FOR UPDATE` on cases first, tasks→cases lock order, one aggregate query (no N+1), subsumes the old `addTasks` NEW→IN_PROGRESS flip, never sets COMPLETED, never touches REVOKED. Any non-COMPLETED move NULLs the verdict columns → re-open invalidation. Test `:158-191` proves a 2nd task re-opens a COMPLETED case → IN_PROGRESS + `verificationOutcome === null`. Discharges design F3 (TOCTOU: status-guarded UPDATE) — though see INFO-2. ✓
- **Audit folded** into the finalize tx (`appendAudit` action `UPDATE`, in-tx). RBAC: `case.finalize` seeded for BACKEND_USER in 0052 + `ROLE_PERMISSIONS` (SA via grants_all) — parity holds. ✓

### Design-quality (CaseDetailPage)
- **Tokens-only, no hardcoded colors.** `CASE_STATUS_TONE` uses `st-*` tokens; verified `st-under-review`/`-bg` are REAL tokens defined in `@crm2/ui-theme/tailwind-preset.js:50` (not invented here; also used by VerificationUnitsPage). AWAITING_COMPLETION→under-review tone is sensible. ✓
- **UPPERCASE display** via `CASE_STATUS_LABELS` + the global CSS transform (labels are Title-case strings, screen-uppercased) — consistent with house pattern. ✓
- **Finalize form gated correctly:** the Case Result card shows only for `COMPLETED || AWAITING_COMPLETION`; the editable `CaseFinalizeForm` shows only when `AWAITING_COMPLETION && canFinalize`; a non-finalizer in AWAITING sees the read-only "awaiting verdict" line; COMPLETED shows the read-only verdict (Verdict/Remark/Finalized-by/Finalized-at). State+perm gating is exactly right. STALE→reload hint, FAILED→generic. ✓

### Plausibility of the DB-auditor's live HTTP + browser E2E PASS
Plausible from the code: routes mount, SDK `cases.finalize` + types compile against the new columns, the read model (`CASE_VIEW_SELECT`) selects `verification_outcome/result_remark/completed_at/version` + `completed_by_name` join, and the test path drives ASSIGNED→COMPLETE→AWAITING→finalize over real HTTP. Migration is strict-superset (no data migration) so an existing dev DB takes it cleanly. Nothing in the diff would break a booted server or the case-detail render.

### FLAG (minor — does not block)
- **F1 · LOW · `recomputeCaseStatus` degenerate all-REVOKED branch → IN_PROGRESS.** When every task is REVOKED/CANCELLED (total>0, active=0, completed=0) the ladder returns IN_PROGRESS for a case with no live work — a slightly odd resting state (the comment acknowledges "degenerate; office handles"). Design §3 said all-tasks-REVOKED does NOT auto-revoke (correct, M1), but parking it at IN_PROGRESS rather than leaving it where it was is a cosmetic oddity, not a correctness defect (office can revisit/revoke; verdict is NULLed safely). **Disposition: ACCEPT for slice 1; carry as a nicety — consider leaving status untouched in the all-terminal-non-completed case.**

### INFO
- **INFO-1 · per-task result is recorded via `/complete` here, not a separate "record result" call.** The test sets the per-task `verification_outcome` through the existing complete path (`result: 'POSITIVE'`), matching spec §2's "desk-complete may also set the per-task result in the same call." The standalone "record result on an already-COMPLETED task" action (§2 row) is not exercised in this slice — acceptable, the column + read model are in place.
- **INFO-2 · design-F3 second limb (can a task be revoked under a COMPLETED case?) is moot in slice 1** — no task-revoke endpoint ships until slice 3. The finalize UPDATE is status-guarded, so the finalize-side TOCTOU is closed; the revoke-side question is correctly deferred to the slice-3 spec. No action now.

### Design OPEN items discharged by this slice
- F2/F4 (multi-leg / demote-vs-keep) → owner kept the per-task column AND added the distinct case verdict; the test proves both coexist. CLOSED for the result-model shape (multi-leg *worst-of vs free-choice* rule is office free-choice by construction — owner-accepted).
- F3 (finalize TOCTOU) → status+OCC-guarded UPDATE. CLOSED (revoke-side deferred, INFO-2).
- F1 commission, F5 AWAITING SLA, F6 device delta → correctly NOT in slice 1 (slices 2/5).

**Bottom line:** PASS — clear to commit. The slice is a faithful, minimal implementation of the two-track spine: single-layer field, per-task office result preserved AND a distinct one-final-case-verdict, single rollup writer with anti-staleness, case-grain scope + OCC + transition guards all real and adversarially tested, commission correctly deferred (not mis-placed), zero scope creep, tokens-only UI with correct state+perm gating. One cosmetic FLAG (all-REVOKED→IN_PROGRESS resting state) carried as a nicety; nothing blocks.
