## 2026-06-15 — slice-2a/2b commit review (ADR-0032 Pipeline-SLA + dashboard lifecycle; tasks repo/service + dashboard repo + SDK `tasks.ts`/`dashboard.ts` + web `PipelinePage.tsx`/`DashboardPage.tsx`/`CounterBar.tsx` + 2 api tests; working tree) — VERDICT: **BLOCK** (1 BLOCK, 0 must-fix, 2 FLAG-minor, 2 INFO)

Adversarial per-commit read of the full `git diff` against the owner's three asks. The lifecycle/SLA modelling is genuinely good — one real product-hole blocks: a dead deep-link from the dashboard's headline office queue.

### The three owner asks — 2 of 3 land clean, the 3rd ships a dead link
- **(1) Pipeline Cancelled→Revoked — DONE.** `PipelinePage.tsx:43` bucket is now `{ label: 'Revoked', status: 'REVOKED', stat: 'revoked' }`; SDK `TaskStats.cancelled`→`revoked` (`tasks.ts:50`); repo stats now FILTER `status='REVOKED'` (`repository.ts:147`); service drops the old `by.get('CANCELLED')` map. ✓ (residual `CANCELLED` key kept in `STATUS_TONE` `PipelinePage.tsx:34` is harmless dead tone — see FLAG-1.)
- **(2) Out-of-TAT bucket — DONE + mutually-exclusive + row badge.** New `{ label: 'Out of TAT', sla: true, stat: 'outOfTat' }` bucket; `selectBucket` (`PipelinePage.tsx:60`) deletes BOTH `status` and `outOfTat` before setting one → status buckets and SLA bucket are truly mutually exclusive; active-state at `:205` (`b.sla ? outOfTat : !outOfTat && status===…`) is correct (selecting SLA de-highlights All/status). Row `⚠ TAT` badge at `:142-150` renders when `t.outOfTat`. Server: `SLA_BREACH_SQL` (`tasks/repository.ts:11`) is a param-free pure-SQL predicate, used identically as the list filter (`buildWhere:107`), the `out_of_tat` SELECT column (`:61`) and the `outOfTat` stat (`:153`) — one definition, three call-sites, no drift. Test `tasks.api.test.ts:365` proves count+filter+flag and that COMPLETED clears it. ✓
- **(3) Dashboard cards — PARTIAL.** Old inert task-level "Awaiting Review" (SUBMITTED_FOR_REVIEW) correctly retired from BOTH the KPI grid (`DashboardPage.tsx:61` now "Out of TAT" → `/pipeline?outOfTat=1`, `tone="alert"`) AND the CounterBar (`CounterBar.tsx:14` now "Awaiting Completion" / `AWAITING_COMPLETION` / `st-under-review` dot). Server `awaitingCompletion` is a correct CASE-grain query (`dashboard/repository.ts:127` `cases.status='AWAITING_COMPLETION'` under `caseScopePredicate`) — the office completion queue, not a task count. Modelling is right. **But the link is dead — see BLOCK-1.**

### BLOCK
- **B-1 · HIGH · `CounterBar.tsx:18` "Awaiting Completion" deep-links to `/cases?status=AWAITING_COMPLETION`, which lands the Cases list UNFILTERED.** The owner's lens explicitly required this card to "link to the CASE queue, not the task pipeline" — the intent is honored (it points at `/cases`, the right surface), but the URL contract is wrong. `CasesPage.tsx` never reads `searchParams` and passes NO `filters` prop to its DataGrid; the only mechanism that pre-applies a column filter is the DataGrid's `f_<id>` key reader (`DataGrid.tsx:222` `params.get('f_${c.id}')`). So `?status=AWAITING_COMPLETION` is an unrecognised key → the grid renders ALL cases, not the awaiting-completion queue. Contrast Pipeline, where `PipelinePage` *bridges* `?status=`/`?outOfTat=1` into the `filters` prop (`:235`) — Cases has no such bridge. The single highest-value office workflow card silently no-ops its filter. **FIX (smallest correct):** change the link to `/cases?f_status=AWAITING_COMPLETION` (the `status` column is `filterable` with `AWAITING_COMPLETION` in `STATUS_OPTIONS`, so the grid will honor it). Re-verify in-browser that the deep-link lands a filtered grid (memory rule: don't stop at code — perform the click). Until then this ask is not delivered.

### FLAG (minor — do not block)
- **F1 · LOW · dead `CANCELLED` entry left in `PipelinePage.tsx:34` `STATUS_TONE`.** Cancelled is gone from buckets/stats; the tone map still carries `CANCELLED: 'bg-st-rejected-bg …'`. Harmless (no task carries that status under the new lifecycle) but it's orphaned-by-this-change dead code per the surgical-changes rule. Drop it. (`REVOKED` tone was correctly added alongside.)
- **F2 · LOW · SLA thresholds duplicated across two module-local constants** (`tasks/repository.ts:11` `SLA_BREACH_SQL` and `dashboard/repository.ts:25` `SLA_BREACH`) with the same 12/24/48/72h ladder. Both carry a comment acknowledging the mirror "to respect module boundaries" — defensible (the dashboard/tasks modules don't share a SQL fragment lib), and both are clearly labelled constants "pending an SLA-config feature," which satisfies the owner's "must be a constant the owner can change" requirement. **Disposition: ACCEPT** — but RATCHET: when the owner-configurable SLA lands, these two must move to one source. If they ever diverge, the dashboard "Out of TAT" KPI and the Pipeline bucket will disagree — a silent MIS-credibility bug.

### INFO
- **INFO-1 · SLA default is reasonable and owner-informed.** URGENT 12h/HIGH 24h/MEDIUM 48h/LOW 72h, unknown→48h, measured from `created_at`. Both copies use the same `ELSE 48h` fallback. Correctly excludes terminal tasks: predicate is gated `status IN ('PENDING','ASSIGNED','IN_PROGRESS')` → COMPLETED and REVOKED can never be out-of-TAT (test asserts COMPLETED clears it). Note: SUBMITTED_FOR_REVIEW is NOT in the OPEN set here — correct under the two-track model (that status is retired; if any legacy rows linger they're simply never SLA-flagged, acceptable).
- **INFO-2 · scope creep — NONE.** No 2c ingest spine: grep of the diff shows no `/start`, `/sync`, `/attachments`, ingest, or device-delta additions. Every changed line traces to one of the three asks (Cancelled→Revoked, Out-of-TAT bucket+badge+stat, dashboard card swap). The `stats()` refactor from GROUP-BY-rows to a single conditional-aggregate row is in-scope (it's what makes the cross-status `outOfTat` count computable in one query) and the test was updated in lockstep. Clean slice.

### Design-quality (UI)
Tokens-only confirmed: `⚠ TAT` badge uses `bg-st-rejected-bg`/`text-st-rejected`, CounterBar dot uses `bg-st-under-review`, dashboard KPI uses `tone="alert"` — all real tokens (`ui-theme/tailwind-preset.js:50,52`), no hex. UPPERCASE display preserved via existing `.replace(/_/g,' ')` + house CSS transform. Mutually-exclusive bucket UX and `replace:true` page re-anchor are correct.

### Carried forward
- B-1 must be fixed + browser-verified before this slice ships.
- F2 RATCHET: collapse the two SLA constants to one source when the configurable-SLA feature lands.
- F1 nit: drop orphaned `CANCELLED` tone.

**Bottom line:** BLOCK. Asks (1) and (2) are clean, well-tested, tokens-only, mutually-exclusive, and scope-disciplined; the SLA model is correct (terminal tasks excluded, sensible owner-informed constant). Ask (3) is modelled correctly server-side but ships a **dead deep-link** — the dashboard's headline "Awaiting Completion" office queue points at `/cases?status=…`, a key the Cases grid does not read, so it lands unfiltered. One-line fix (`f_status=`) + an in-browser click to confirm a filtered grid clears the block. Two minor FLAGs (orphaned CANCELLED tone; duplicated SLA constant — accept now, ratchet later).

## 2026-06-15 — slice-2c-1 commit review (ADR-0032 field-execution ingest spine; new `verification-tasks` module [routes/controller/service/test] + 4 device writers in `cases/repository.ts` + migration `0053_task_execute_perm.sql` + `@crm2/access` `TASK_EXECUTE` + 3 parity-test updates + app wiring + openapi; working tree) — VERDICT: **PASS** (0 BLOCK, 0 must-fix, 1 FLAG-minor, 2 INFO)

Adversarial per-commit read of `git diff` + the new module against the owner's five lenses. This slice is disciplined and coherent — it delivers a real start→complete vertical that flows into the lifecycle, with ownership enforced server-side. No blocker.

### (a) Coherent vertical — DELIVERED.
`POST /api/v2/verification-tasks/:id/{start,complete,revoke}` + `PUT /:id/priority` (`routes.ts:12-15`), all gated `task.execute`. Service binds ownership: `ownedCaseId` → `repo.taskForAssignee(taskId, actorId)` resolves the task IFF `assigned_to = actor` else 404 (`service.ts:20-24`, `repository.ts` `taskForAssignee`) — IDOR-safe, ownership enforced beyond the perm. `completeTaskByDevice` runs `recomputeCaseStatus` (`repository.ts` complete writer), and the rollup ladder (`repository.ts:103-110`) correctly lands the case at AWAITING_COMPLETION when no active tasks remain — the exact handoff the office finalize (slice 1, `repository.ts:760` guards `status='AWAITING_COMPLETION'`) consumes. Live E2E (start→IN_PROGRESS→complete→COMPLETED→case AWAITING_COMPLETION + non-owner 404) confirms the wire. ✓

### (b) Owner-decision fidelity (D1/D2) — HONORED.
Field records NO result: no `verification_outcome`/`result_remark` write in any device writer; complete writer's doc-comment and test (`verification-tasks.api.test.ts:100,108` assert `verificationOutcome` null after both start and complete) prove single-layer. The device never sees a review state — there is no SUBMITTED_FOR_REVIEW in this path; complete == COMPLETED (D2). The office still owns the per-task result + the one case verdict via slice 1. ✓

### (c) Migration 0053 — forward-only + idempotent + correct grant.
`INSERT … ('FIELD_AGENT','task.execute') ON CONFLICT (role_code, permission_code) DO NOTHING` in a BEGIN/COMMIT — re-runnable, no seed-drift. It seeds `task.execute`→FIELD_AGENT ONLY (NOT case.finalize — correct, finalize stays BACKEND_USER/SA), mirroring `@crm2/access` `ROLE_PERMISSIONS.FIELD_AGENT` (`permissions.ts:100`). Parity tests updated consistently in lockstep — exact-list assertions now `['case.view','location.capture','task.execute']` in all 3 suites (access `access.api.test.ts:35`, auth login+me `auth.api.test.ts:84,88`, roles seed `roles.api.test.ts:16`). **Triple-write verified live:** dev `crm2_dev`@54329 AND test `crm2_test`@5433 both return `FIELD_AGENT / task.execute`; `case_tasks` carries `started_at,completed_by,version,priority` on both — the device writers' columns all exist. ✓

### (c-scope) Scope creep — NONE.
grep of the new module + device writers for `attachment|form_submission|sync.?delta|photo|commission|upload` → zero hits. openapi diff adds ONLY `/api/v2/verification-tasks` paths. No commission in the device path (correct — commission gates on office COMPLETED, ADR-0032 §7; revoke writer explicitly records none). Stays exactly within start/complete/revoke/priority + the perm; form-submit/attachments/sync-delta correctly deferred to 2c-2. ✓

### FLAG (minor — do not block)
- **F1 · LOW · revoke reason is captured but NOT yet office-readable.** Per design the reason rides the audit row (`appendAudit … after:{status:'REVOKED', reason}`, revoke writer) with no `case_tasks` column — acceptable for an ingest slice. BUT: there is no v2 audit-read endpoint, and `CaseTaskView` (`packages/sdk/src/cases.ts:147`) carries no `reason` field, so today the office cannot see WHY a task was device-revoked through any API — the datum exists only in `audit_log.after.reason`. Capture-now/surface-later is fine for 2c-1; **RATCHET:** before device-revoke is used operationally, a reason-read path (audit-read endpoint or a `CaseTaskView.revokeReason` projection) must ship, else the office sees a REVOKED task with no rationale. Not a blocker for the ingest spine.

### INFO
- **INFO-1 · idempotency semantics are correct and consistent with the contract.** start/complete/revoke are idempotent-as-success (re-fire from the terminal-target state → 200 with current row; an illegal source → 409 INVALID_TRANSITION), matching "device treats 409 as success" only where intended. priority is deliberately NOT idempotent-as-success: a terminal task → 409 (`setTaskPriorityByDevice` returns no row → conflict; test `:135` asserts 409). All four writers bump `version` (web OCC preserved) though the device sends none. Each transition is guarded in the WHERE (`status IN (...)`), so concurrent/out-of-order device retries can't corrupt state. The `$2::uuid` cast on `assigned_to` and the controller's strict UUID regex (`controller.ts:6-9`, 400 on malformed id) close the bad-input edge.
- **INFO-2 · rollup safety.** complete/revoke run `recomputeCaseStatus`; start does not (ASSIGNED→IN_PROGRESS keeps the case active — no bucket change, correctly skipped). Rollup never sets COMPLETED, never touches a REVOKED case (`:89,95`), and clears stale verdict columns on any non-COMPLETED move (anti-staleness) — REVOKED-only degenerate case falls back to IN_PROGRESS for the office, acceptable.

### Carried forward
- F1 RATCHET: ship an office-visible revoke-reason read path before device-revoke goes operational.

## 2026-06-16 — slice-3 commit review (ADR-0033 task lineage — REVISIT + REASSIGN-AFTER-REVOKE + verdict history; migration `0054_task_lineage.sql`, cases repo/service/controller/routes + test, `@crm2/access` `TASK_REWORK`, SDK `cases.ts`/`client.ts`/`cases.test.ts`, web `CaseDetailPage.tsx`, openapi; working tree) — VERDICT: **FLAG** (0 BLOCK, 0 must-fix, 1 FLAG-HIGH, 1 FLAG-low, 3 INFO)

Adversarial per-commit read of the full `git diff` + 0054 migration against ADR-0033 and the owner's 2026-06-15 correction (backend NEVER revokes; reassign-after-revoke full v1 parity; RECHECK collapsed into REVISIT; full verdict-history panel). The slice is faithful, scope-disciplined, and well-tested. One real concurrency gap on the very guard the ADR names as the double-bill defence — FLAG, not BLOCK (needs simultaneous requests; happy path + `pnpm verify` green).

### ADR-0033 fidelity (the lens) — honored
- **Backend-revoke fully removed.** No `task.revoke` perm anywhere; migration comment + `@crm2/access` comment both record the owner correction. The only new perm is `task.rework` → BACKEND_USER + MANAGER (migration `0054:40-43`, `permissions.ts:78,100`), SA via grants_all. Parity tests unaffected: the exact-list assertions pin only FIELD_AGENT (`access/auth/roles` suites); MANAGER uses `toContain` (`roles.api.test.ts:77`). ✓
- **REVISIT (parent COMPLETED → new PENDING REVISIT task, re-opens case, invalidates verdict, billed separately).** Service status-guards COMPLETED→409 INVALID_TRANSITION + blocks 2nd open revisit→409 ACTIVE_REVISIT_EXISTS (`service.ts:359-362`); repo clones CPV+applicant+address+trigger+priority+visit_type+location, born PENDING, `task_origin='REVISIT'`, `parent_task_id` set, runs the single `recomputeCaseStatus` writer to re-open + NULL the verdict (`repository.ts:872-918`). Test `cases.api.test.ts:1024` asserts child REVISIT/PENDING/parentTaskId, case→IN_PROGRESS, `verificationOutcome` null, parent stays COMPLETED/ORIGINAL. ✓
- **REASSIGN-AFTER-REVOKE (parent REVOKED → new ASSIGNED replacement, keeps parent origin, no extra bill).** Service REVOKED→409, eligibility re-checked via the SAME `taskRepository.eligibleTaskIdsForAssignee([taskId],…)` path as a normal reassign →400 INVALID_ASSIGNEE (`service.ts:375-385`); repo clones into a born-ASSIGNED row, `task_origin = p.task_origin` (parent's), writes the ASSIGNED history event with `previous_assigned_to`=revoked assignee (`repository.ts:930-1010`); revoked row never re-activated. Test `:1066` asserts ASSIGNED/assignedTo=v2/parentTaskId/origin ORIGINAL, case→IN_PROGRESS, original stays REVOKED; guard test `:1100` covers non-REVOKED→409, ineligible→400, verifier 403, out-of-scope 404. ✓
- **VERDICT HISTORY (read-only, case.view, IDOR-safe).** `repository.ts:834-849` reads ONLY `entity_type='case'` audit rows with non-null `after_data->>'verificationOutcome'`. Verified the filter is precise: the finalize writer (`:775-784`) is the ONLY `entity_type='case'` row carrying `verificationOutcome` (+`resultRemark`, which the query maps to `remark`); both per-task result writers (`/complete` `:711-720`, `recordTaskResult` `:815-824`) use `entity_type='case_task'` and are excluded; case CREATE (`:302`) has no outcome key. Service visibility-guards via `caseVisible` (404). Test `:1131` asserts newest-first, before/after (POSITIVE→NEGATIVE), actorName resolves for a real BE finalizer, out-of-scope→404. ✓
- **RECHECK collapsed into REVISIT.** `task_origin` CHECK = `('ORIGINAL','REVISIT')` only; SDK `TASK_ORIGINS`, labels, and `cases.test.ts:93` all match. ✓

### Scope discipline — clean
Every changed line traces to revisit / reassign-after-revoke / verdict-history / the `task_origin`+`parent_task_id` projection. No commission wiring (`grep -i commission|bill.*insert` on the new writers = the only `bill_count` is the operator-supplied reassign clone; slice-5 reads `task_origin`, nothing accrues here). No device/mobile path touched. openapi adds exactly the 3 new paths. Migration is forward-only + idempotent (`IF NOT EXISTS`, `DROP CONSTRAINT IF EXISTS` then re-add, `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`), `parent_task_id` ON DELETE NO ACTION (lineage immutable, no delete path). ✓

### Web (CaseDetailPage) — tokens-only, state+perm-gated
- Revisit shows only on COMPLETED, Reassign only on REVOKED, both gated `canRework` (`:471-497`); the ADR-0024 assign button now correctly renders ONLY for PENDING/ASSIGNED (`:425`, the stale `disabled` removed) — terminal tasks route to revisit/reassign instead. The four open-rows (assign/complete/revisit/reassign) are mutually exclusive (each open-handler nulls the others). ✓
- Reassign reuses `AssignForm` (eligible-assignees keyed on the REVOKED task's OWN area/pincode `:616-623`) → FE pool matches the server eligibility check exactly; submits `{assignedTo,visitType,billCount}` (no `version` — correct, it creates a new row, not an OCC update). Revisit uses a tiny optional-reason `ReasonForm`. Verdict-History panel hides until ≥1 finalize, marks the newest `current`. ✓
- Tokens/UPPERCASE: `bg-surface-muted`/`text-muted-foreground`/`text-st-approved`/`text-destructive` — all real tokens, no hex; the REVISIT badge + history labels use the house uppercase-tracking pattern. ✓ (`text-st-approved` for the `current` chip is an existing token, reused.)

### FLAG (HIGH — does not block, but fix before this goes operational)
- **F1 · HIGH · `ACTIVE_REVISIT_EXISTS` guard is TOCTOU-racy — the one guard ADR-0033 names as the double-bill defence can be beaten by two concurrent revisits of the same COMPLETED parent.** `service.revisitTask` calls `repo.hasActiveRevisitOf(taskId)` (`service.ts:362`) — a plain `SELECT count(*)` (`repository.ts:855-863`) — OUTSIDE any transaction/lock, THEN inserts in a separate tx (`repository.ts:872`). Two simultaneous requests (two office users, or a fronted double-click that beats the FE button-disable) both read 0 → both insert a REVISIT child → two open revisits of one parent → exactly the double-bill the ADR's §guard + Consequences "stop double-billing the same completed task" promises to prevent. The partial index `idx_case_tasks_parent` is **NON-unique** (`0054:35`), so the DB does not catch it (contrast the task_number UNIQUE, which IS DB-enforced + caught at `:920`). This is the same TOCTOU class the slice-1 finalize correctly closed with a status-guarded UPDATE + OCC; revisit has no equivalent. **FIX (smallest correct):** either (a) `SELECT … FROM case_tasks WHERE id=$parent FOR UPDATE` on the parent at the top of the revisit tx and re-run the active-revisit check INSIDE the tx, or (b) a partial UNIQUE index `(parent_task_id) WHERE task_origin='REVISIT' AND status IN ('PENDING','ASSIGNED','IN_PROGRESS')` and map its violation to 409 ACTIVE_REVISIT_EXISTS. **Disposition: FLAG (not BLOCK)** — the happy path is correct, `pnpm verify` is green, and it requires genuinely concurrent requests; but this MUST be closed before revisit is used operationally, as it directly defeats a billing invariant. Add a concurrency test (two parallel revisits → exactly one 201, one 409).

### FLAG (low)
- **F2 · LOW · reassign-after-revoke has NO duplicate-replacement guard (two concurrent reassigns of one REVOKED parent → two ASSIGNED replacements).** Unlike revisit, there is no `hasActiveReassignOf` check at all (`service.reassignRevokedTask`). ADR-0033 does not mandate one (the replacement keeps the parent's origin → no extra bill, so no billing-invariant breach), but two agents dispatched to redo one revoked task is an operational oddity. **Disposition: ACCEPT for slice 3** — no billing impact, ADR-silent; note for the operator. If real cases hit it, add the same per-parent active-replacement guard (and close it transactionally, per F1).

### INFO
- **INFO-1 · verdict-history actor join is null-safe.** `LEFT JOIN users u ON u.id::text = a.actor_id` → a synthetic SA actor (not in `users`) yields `actorName` null → UI renders 'Unknown' (`CaseDetailPage.tsx`); the test uses a REAL BE finalizer to assert the name resolves. Reasonable.
- **INFO-2 · revisit/reassign task_number generation matches `addTasks` exactly** (`(SELECT case_number …) || '-' || (count(*)+1)`, UNIQUE-guarded, retryable 409 on collision at `:920`/`:1009`). Same concurrency caveat as add-tasks (already accepted in prior ledger), correctly surfaced as TASK_NUMBER_CONFLICT.
- **INFO-3 · reassign clones distance_band/bill_count from operator input, not the parent** (FIELD billing inputs), while `AssignForm` omits `distanceBand` (server `?? null`) — identical to the existing normal-assign behaviour (`:631`), not a regression. The verdict-history `remark` correctly reads `resultRemark` (the finalize writer's key), not `remark`.

### Carried forward
- **F1 (HIGH): close the ACTIVE_REVISIT_EXISTS TOCTOU (FOR UPDATE on parent in-tx, or a partial UNIQUE index) + add a parallel-revisit test BEFORE revisit goes operational.** Defeats the ADR's double-bill guard under concurrency.
- F2 (low): consider a per-parent active-replacement guard for reassign if operationally needed.

**Bottom line:** FLAG. A faithful, scope-disciplined slice 3: backend-revoke fully removed per the owner correction, both office interventions (revisit COMPLETED→new billed PENDING task re-opening the case + invalidating the verdict; reassign REVOKED→new ASSIGNED replacement keeping parent origin/no extra bill) status-guarded + scope-guarded + eligibility-checked, a precise audit-log-derived verdict-history (case-entity + non-null-outcome filter excludes both per-task result writers), tokens-only state/perm-gated UI with the stale ADR-0024 assign button correctly narrowed to PENDING/ASSIGNED, clean migration + parity, thorough adversarial tests. One real defect blocks operational use but not the commit: the `ACTIVE_REVISIT_EXISTS` guard is TOCTOU-racy (check-then-insert outside a lock, non-unique index) and can double-bill under two concurrent revisits — the exact invariant the ADR names; fix transactionally + add a parallel test. One low FLAG (no reassign dup-guard; ADR-silent, no bill impact).

**Bottom line:** PASS. A clean, scope-disciplined vertical: a field agent drives their own assigned task start→complete on /api/v2 and it rolls the case to AWAITING_COMPLETION for the office finalize (slice 1) — verified by live E2E and the 4-test suite (lifecycle/idempotency, revoke+empty-reason 400, priority-409-on-terminal, ownership 404 + RBAC 403). Owner-decision fidelity holds (no field result D1, no device review state D2). Migration 0053 is forward-only + idempotent, grants `task.execute`→FIELD_AGENT only (not finalize), mirrors @crm2/access, parity tests updated in all 3 suites, and triple-write is confirmed on BOTH live DBs. No commission/form/attachment/sync creep. One minor FLAG: the device-revoke reason is captured in the audit row but not surfaced through any API yet — fine for the ingest spine, ratchet before operational use.

- **2026-06-16 · ADR-0034 device FIELD-PHOTO upload (slice 2c-2) — `POST /api/v2/verification-tasks/:id/attachments` (multer + sharp) + mig 0055 + `platform/photo.ts` + SDK `DeviceAttachment*` (working tree, pre-commit).** **VERDICT: PASS (clear to commit).** Audited adversarially; ran the new suite + a live sharp EXIF-strip proof myself rather than rubber-stamp.
  - **Byte-faithful to the LOCKED v1 contract — CONFIRMED against the actual mobile source** (`crm-mobile-native/src/sync/uploaders/AttachmentUploader.ts`), not just the ADR. Request: device posts `files[]` + `photoType`/`operationId`/`clientSha256`/`geoLocation(JSON)` form fields + `Idempotency-Key` header = `operationId` (uploader:166); v2 reads the header first, falls back to the `operationId` field (controller). Response: mobile reads `response.data.attachments[0].id` + `.url` (uploader:185,205) — both present in the SDK `DeviceAttachment` (`url`=storage_key alias, `id`). `{success,message,data:{attachments,failed,caseId,taskId,verificationType,submissionId}}` envelope is the device shape (isolated to this endpoint, not the v2 list envelope) — correct per ADR. **200-on-replay (NOT 409-as-success)** — and the device explicitly fears the v1 body-hash `409 IDEMPOTENCY_KEY_CONFLICT` DLQ-trap (uploader:117-123); v2's operationId-keyed 200 replay is strictly safer. Mobile uploads ONE file/op (`attachments?.[0]`) and gates on `response.success` (=`attachments.length>0`) → a single-file failure → success=false → device retries. Faithful.
  - **GEO/EXIF no-leak — PROVEN, not asserted.** Ran the exact pipeline (`sharp(bytes).rotate().toBuffer()`) on a JPEG carrying 206B of EXIF incl. GPS: stored artifact `exif:false` (gone), format preserved. Geo survives ONLY in the structured `geo_location` jsonb column. The stored evidence image has no GPS. Server sha256 is taken of the STRIPPED bytes (`sha256(stripped)`, service) = the IT-Act evidence hash; client hash validated `^[0-9a-f]{64}$` (else null), `hashVerified` logged-not-rejected on mismatch (rollout safety). ✔.
  - **Scope/standards — clean.** New deps multer+sharp both in ALLOWED_DEPENDENCIES (CTO/ADR-0034) + @types/multer; multer memoryStorage only, bounded `files:20` + `fileSize:MAX_ATTACHMENT_BYTES` (reuses the 25MiB constant — no magic number); UPPERCASE consts (`MAX_FIELD_FILES`/`SHA256_RE`/`UNIQUE_VIOLATION`); tokens N/A (BE). Mig 0055 forward-only + idempotent (every ADD COLUMN/INDEX `IF NOT EXISTS`, CHECK dropped-then-readded), extends `case_attachments` in place w/ `kind` discriminator (OFFICE_REF default backfills office rows untouched) + partial-UNIQUE on operation_id. Magic-byte `detectAttachment` gate rejects non-images per-file; storageKey uses the detected ext; sharp keeps source format so mimeType stays coherent. Per-file errors → `failed[]`; only `STORAGE_NOT_CONFIGURED` (503) re-thrown to fail the whole request (a real transient S3 put error falls to failed[] — matches "only a 503 fails the request"). UNIQUE_VIOLATION race → re-reads + returns the cached set (idempotent under concurrency).
  - **Gate:** new suite 7/7 PASS incl. both ADR-0034 cases (upload+replay-idempotent+server/client hash+FIELD_PHOTO row; non-assignee 404 / missing-key 400 / non-image→success=false failed[]). Prompt states full `pnpm verify` green api 618/618 + live MinIO E2E + replay; single-file run shows the expected coverage-threshold artifact only.
  - **OPEN / FLAG (non-blocking, ratchet):**
    - **F1 (low, doc drift):** ALLOWED_DEPENDENCIES.md + ADR-0034 both say sharp is "lazy-imported in `platform/image`" — the actual file is `platform/photo.ts`. Cosmetic; fix the two doc refs.
    - **F2 (low, orphaned object):** if the THUMBNAIL `put` throws a non-503 error after the main `put` succeeded but before the DB insert, the main stripped object is left in storage with no DB row (per-file → failed[], no DB leak, evidence not lost-but-unreferenced). Latent; device uploads 1 file/op so retry re-stores under a fresh UUID key. Consider inserting the row before the thumbnail put, or a GC sweep — ratchet, not a blocker.
    - **F3 (low, multi-file partial replay):** a multi-file op that partially stores then a file fails → retry sees the partial set via `fieldAttachmentsByOperation` and returns it as cached with `failed:[]`, never retrying the failed file. Does NOT bite the device (1 file/op). Ratchet only if the endpoint ever serves true multi-file batches.

**Bottom line:** PASS. A faithful, scope-disciplined completion of the field-execution ingest spine: the locked v1 multipart photo contract is reproduced byte-for-byte on /api/v2 (verified against the real mobile uploader, not just the ADR), 200-on-replay deliberately avoids the v1 body-hash 409 DLQ-trap, ownership-bound (404) + task.execute-gated, and the GPS/EXIF leak is provably closed — stored bytes carry no metadata, geo lives only in the structured column, and the server hashes the stripped artifact as the legal evidence hash. Migration is forward-only/idempotent and reuses one attachments table via a clean `kind` discriminator. Three low ratchets (doc-path drift; thumbnail-fail orphan object; multi-file partial-replay) — none block the commit; the device's 1-file-per-op reality neutralizes the two semantic ones. No 409-as-success, no scope creep, no magic numbers.

## 2026-06-16 — slice-2c-2 tail commit review (ADR-0035 sync delta arrays + execution fields; `sync/repository.ts` [+`startedAt/completedAt` on SyncTaskRow+SYNC_SELECT, new `revokedAssignmentIdsForUser`] + `sync/service.ts` [`toMobileTask`→`inProgressAt/completedAt`; `download()` offset-0 `revokedAssignmentIds`] + mig `0057_task_assignment_history_prev_idx.sql` + `sync.api.test.ts` +5 + ADR-0035; working tree) — VERDICT: **PASS** (0 BLOCK, 0 must-fix, 1 FLAG-low, 3 INFO)

Adversarial per-line read of the diff + the 4 `task_assignment_history` writers + the `cases` read-model filter, against ADR-0035's three claims (disjoint upsert/purge sets, offset-0 delta safety, no-formData-echo). Re-ran the suite against a real Postgres (13/13 incl. the 5 new) AND wrote a throwaway probe to empirically test the one scenario the diff does NOT cover — reassign-after-revoke. Found one real false-positive (harmless on the device, but a cross-agent info leak) — FLAG, not BLOCK.

### ADR-0035 fidelity — the three claims
- **Claim 1 (disjoint upsert/purge: current `assigned_to=me` `cases` vs `≠me` purge) — HOLDS for the device's own rows, but the purge set is NOT strictly "tasks I once held" (see F1).** The `cases` read filter is `ct.assigned_to = $me` (`sync/repository.ts:85`); the purge query is `previous_assigned_to=$me AND ct.assigned_to IS DISTINCT FROM $me` (`:118-120`). For a row the device actually has, the two are mutually exclusive by the `assigned_to` predicate — no upsert/purge race. **Reassigned-then-back (A→B→A) is correctly EXCLUDED**: the `IS DISTINCT FROM current` clause (joining history→live `case_tasks`) returns FALSE when current=A, so it flows via `cases`, never purged — verified the DISTINCT-FROM-current is what saves it, not a created_at trick. ✓
- **Claim 2 (REVOKED-but-still-mine is NOT a purge) — CONFIRMED in code + live.** Revoke writer (`cases/repository.ts:1124`) sets `status='REVOKED'` and KEEPS `assigned_to` → row stays in `cases` with `isRevoked=true`, absent from the purge set. Test `:147` proves exactly this (revoke own task → `revokedAssignmentIds:[]`, `cases[0].isRevoked=true`). ✓
- **Claim 3 (no `formData` echo) — CONFIRMED.** `toMobileTask` emits NO `formData` key; SDK declares `formData?` optional but it is never populated; test `:171` asserts `task.formData` undefined. `isSaved` stays hardcoded `false` (`:47`). Correct — the device owns its draft, no blind-overwrite vector. ✓

### Execution fields + envelope — correct
- `inProgressAt`(←`started_at`)/`completedAt`(←`completed_at`) emitted additively, **omitted when null** via the `...(x?{}:{})` spread (`service.ts:36-37`) → v1 byte-wire preserved when unset. `iso()` only ever sees a DB timestamp (non-null guarded) so no throw. Test `:160` proves both undefined pre-start, both ISO strings post start+complete, and `completedAt >= inProgressAt`. ✓
- **Envelope NOT normalized to v2 `Paginated<T>`** — test `:179` pins the exact `{success,message,data}` top level + all 10 `data` keys + asserts `items/total/page` undefined. Genuinely guards the locked device contract against a future list-envelope refactor. ✓
- **No SDK contract change** (all fields pre-declared optional in `packages/sdk/src/sync.ts:41,53,70`) → no OpenAPI surface change, as the ADR claims. Mig 0057 is forward-only + idempotent (`CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS`), and the composite `(previous_assigned_to, created_at)` is an exact match for the query predicate — no seq-scan on the unbounded append-only history. ✓

### offset-0-only delta — NOT a correctness risk (today)
The device persists its watermark only after a FULL cycle and restarts every cycle at offset 0 (ADR §5, the kickoff's device-consumer audit). So offset-0 always sees the delta; pages >0 within one cycle correctly return `[]` (test `:391` proves page-0=`[taskId]`, page-1=`[]`). The device-side purge is idempotent + `recentlyCleaned`-deduped, so even a redundant re-emit would be harmless. **The one latent trap is correctly captured as the ADR's CARRY**: if the device ever resumes from offset>0 mid-cycle, the delta is missed — revisit on any device cycle-semantics change. Acceptable; not a today-bug. ✓

### Scope / verify
Every changed line traces to ADR-0035 (two execution fields + one delta array + its supporting index + 5 tests). No `formData`/attachment/commission/route creep. Re-ran `sync.api.test.ts` against real PG@54329 (template-cloned, picks up 0057): **13/13 PASS** incl. all 5 new. Prompt's full-verify-green (typecheck 8/8, build, api 624/624) + live :4000 E2E corroborated and plausible from the code. ✓

### FLAG (low — does not block)
- **F1 · LOW · `revokedAssignmentIds` carries a FALSE-POSITIVE under reassign-after-revoke: the OLD assignee A is handed the NEW replacement task's UUID — a task A was never assigned.** EMPIRICALLY PROVEN (throwaway probe, since added, run, and reverted): A revokes own task `T` → office reassign-after-revoke creates a NEW task `T'` assigned to B, and `reassignRevokedTask` (`cases/repository.ts:989-992`) writes `T'`'s first history row with `previous_assigned_to = parent.assignedTo = A` (the revoked assignee). The sync delta then matches `previous_assigned_to=A AND T'.assigned_to=B IS DISTINCT FROM A` → **A's `revokedAssignmentIds` = [T']**, while A's revoked original `T` correctly stays in A's `cases` (`isRevoked=true`). **Device impact: NONE** — A never synced `T'` (distinct UUID, born ASSIGNED to B), so the device's `verification_task_id`-keyed purge is a no-op on a row A doesn't have (idempotent). **But it IS a defect of intent + a minor cross-agent info-leak:** the array's contract is "tasks I once held," yet it discloses to A the UUID + existence of B's replacement task on the same case. The root cause is the reassign writer reusing the parent's old assignee as the NEW row's `previous_assigned_to` (a lineage convenience), which the prev-assignee-keyed delta query cannot distinguish from a genuine reassign-away. **FIX (smallest correct):** narrow the delta query so the matched history row is the one that ACTUALLY moved the device user OFF a task they held — e.g. `AND h.assigned_to IS DISTINCT FROM $1` (the reassign-after-revoke row has `assigned_to=B`, `previous=A`; but a genuine reassign-away of A's live task to B ALSO has `assigned_to=B,previous=A` on the SAME task A held — so that alone won't separate them). The clean discriminator is **the task identity**: the genuine-away event and the `cases`-resident row share `task_id`; the false-positive's `task_id` (=T') is one A never held. Restrict to history rows whose `task_id` the user has a NON-`previous`-only footprint on, OR (simpler) exclude rows where the SAME `task_id` has a later `previous_assigned_to=A`→no… — practically: filter the delta to `task_id`s where A was ever the `assigned_to` (`EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM task_assignment_history h2 WHERE h2.task_id=h.task_id AND h2.assigned_to=$1)`), which T' fails (A was never assigned T'). **Disposition: FLAG (not BLOCK)** — happy path + all 5 ADR tests green, the device is provably unaffected (no-op purge), and reassign-after-revoke is an office-initiated low-frequency path; but close it before this is leaned on operationally, and add a reassign-after-revoke test asserting the OLD assignee's `revokedAssignmentIds` does NOT contain the replacement task.

### INFO
- **INFO-1 · the disjoint-set test coverage has a gap the diff's own tests don't reach.** The 5 new tests cover plain reassign-away, revoke-still-mine, exec fields, envelope, offset-0 — but NOT reassign-AFTER-revoke (the F1 path). That's the one combination where the two `task_assignment_history` write-sites (assign/reassign on the live task vs the clone-with-parent's-assignee in `reassignRevokedTask`) interact with the delta query. Recommend a regression test there regardless of whether F1 is fixed now.
- **INFO-2 · cutoff is shared between the row query and the delta query** (both use the same `cutoff`), which is correct: a reassign-away event older than the device's watermark was already delivered in the cycle that covered it (the device persists the watermark only post-full-cycle), so re-emitting it isn't required and the device purge is idempotent anyway. No staleness window introduced.
- **INFO-3 · `deletedTaskIds`/`deletedCaseIds` stay `[]` — verified there is genuinely no hard delete path** (`grep` of cases/verification-tasks writers shows status transitions only, never `DELETE FROM case_tasks/cases`; `parent_task_id` is `ON DELETE NO ACTION` per slice-3). The placeholder arrays are honest, not a stub-left-behind.

### Carried forward
- **F1 (low): close the reassign-after-revoke false-positive** (restrict the delta to `task_id`s the user was ever `assigned_to`, not merely `previous_assigned_to`) + add the regression test (INFO-1) before `revokedAssignmentIds` is relied on for cross-agent hygiene. Cross-agent UUID disclosure, not a device-state corruption.
- ADR CARRY (offset-0-only) stands: revisit if the device ever resumes a cycle from offset>0.

**Bottom line:** PASS — clear to commit. A disciplined, byte-faithful slice: execution timestamps emitted additively (omitted-when-null preserves the v1 wire), `revokedAssignmentIds` wired to the append-only history with an exact-match supporting index, the two ADR invariants that matter on the device — REVOKED-but-mine flows via `cases` not purge, and `formData` is never echoed — both confirmed in code AND live, the locked envelope explicitly guarded against a `Paginated` refactor, offset-0-only delta correct under the device's known cycle semantics (latent risk honestly carried). Suite re-run green against real Postgres (13/13). One real but non-blocking defect found by going past the shipped tests: under reassign-after-revoke the old assignee receives the replacement task's UUID in `revokedAssignmentIds` — harmless on the device (no-op purge of a never-held row) but a contract-intent miss + minor cross-agent info-leak; narrow the delta to tasks the user was actually `assigned_to` and add the missing regression test before operational reliance.

---

## 2026-06-16 — slice-5a commit review (ADR-0036 billing & commission model — the `commission_rates` config foundation; NEW migration `0058_commission_rates.sql` + NEW `commissionRates` module [repository/service/controller/routes + api.test] + `@crm2/sdk` `commissionRates.ts` (+test, index, client, client.test) + app mount + openapi; working tree, UNCOMMITTED) — VERDICT: **PASS** (0 BLOCK, 0 must-fix, 2 FLAG-low, 2 INFO)

Adversarial read of the full new module + 0058 against ADR-0036's five decisions, side-by-side against the `rates` module it claims to mirror, plus a scope-honesty sweep ("is this really config-only, engine later?"). The slice is faithful, tight, and scope-disciplined — it ships exactly the config table + CRUD + one resolver seam, no engine. No blocker. Two low FLAGs on test-claim-vs-coverage and the lone forward-hook.

### ADR-0036 fidelity (the lens) — honored
- **D3 · config master-data, modelled exactly like `rates`.** Mig 0058: effective-dated (`effective_from`/`effective_to`), OCC `version` default 1 (ADR-0019), GiST no-overlap EXCLUDE on `(user_id =, rate_type =, COALESCE(client_id,-1) =, tstzrange(from, COALESCE(to,'infinity'),'[)') &&) WHERE (is_active)` — the universal-as-`-1` coalesce + half-open range exactly match the `rates_no_overlap` idiom; `idx_commission_rates_resolve (user_id, rate_type, client_id) WHERE is_active`. Forward-only + idempotent (`CREATE TABLE/INDEX/EXTENSION IF NOT EXISTS`, constraint added via `pg_constraint` existence guard). Gated `page.masterdata` (read) / `masterdata.manage` (write) — `routes.ts` reuses the exact `PERMISSIONS.MASTERDATA_VIEW/MANAGE` constants `rates` uses, **no new permission** (verified `permissions.ts:19-20`). ✓
- **D1/D2 · ANY user may hold rates + most-specific-client-wins resolver.** `resolveAmount(user, rateType, client)` → `WHERE user_id AND rate_type AND is_active AND (client_id IS NULL OR client_id=$3) AND effective_from<=now() AND (effective_to IS NULL OR effective_to>now()) ORDER BY client_id DESC NULLS LAST LIMIT 1` — client-scoped row (client_id=N) sorts before universal (NULL) under DESC NULLS LAST, so client wins; null return when unconfigured (NOT an error). Temporal predicate uses DB `now()` (skew-proof, consistent with the list view + ADR-0036 Consequences). No eligibility/role filter on who may hold a row — any user. ✓
- **D4 · derived now, engine later — CONFIRMED scope-honest.** grep of the whole repo for `resolveAmount` callers OUTSIDE the module + its own test = **NONE** (redirected-tmpdir grep, clean). No `case_tasks.billed`/`billed_at`, no invoice/payout/GST, no PENDING→APPROVED→PAID, no financial-summary card, no v1 FUCA touch (`git status` shows zero collateral billing/invoice/fuca files). openapi adds EXACTLY the 5 `/api/v2/commission-rates` paths, nothing else. The only "engine-adjacent" line is the `resolveAmount` seam — see F2. ✓
- **Revise = effective-dated, self-historizing (no history table).** `revise` runs in `withTransaction` + `FOR UPDATE` on the parent: version-check (→`AppError.stale`) → active-check (→409 `COMMISSION_RATE_NOT_ACTIVE`) → end-date the current row FIRST (`effective_to=COALESCE($eff,now())`, version+1) → INSERT the new dated row. The end-date-before-insert + half-open `[)` range means old `[from, eff)` and new `[eff, ∞)` don't overlap at the boundary even though both are `is_active` under the EXCLUDE's `WHERE (is_active)` — the test (revise→200, no 409) proves it empirically. ✓

### Mirroring `rates` — the right call, and faithfully done
The module is a near-mechanical clone of `rates`' shape (same `COLS`/`float8` cast, same `mapWriteError`(`23P01`→domain-409, `23503`→`INVALID_REFERENCE`), same `PageSpec` sort/filter-map + `resolvePage`/`buildPage`, same OCC `requireVersion`+`AppError.stale` flow, same controller try/next + `parseId` integer-guard). Mirroring is correct here: `commission_rates` is the same KIND of object (effective-dated, OCC, no-overlap masterdata) and reusing the proven idiom is lower-risk than inventing a parallel one. **One deliberate, correct divergence:** `setActive` is NOT wrapped in `withTransaction` (rates' is) — because rates' tx exists only to co-write a `rate_history` side-row on deactivate, and commission_rates is self-historizing (no history table), so there's no second write to make atomic; the `WHERE … AND version=$4` is the authoritative OCC guard and the prior plain `SELECT` only supplies the 404-vs-stale `before` snapshot. Benign read-then-write (the read is non-authoritative), no TOCTOU on a billing invariant. ✓

### Naming — clean
`commission_rates` / `commissionRates` / `COMMISSION_RATE_EXISTS` / `COMMISSION_RATE_NOT_ACTIVE` / `COMMISSION_RATE_NOT_FOUND` are consistent and self-describing; `rate_type` reuses the `rates.rate_type` code vocabulary (LOCAL/OGL/…) per the SDK comment, so the two engines share a tier vocabulary — correct for a later joined billing view. SDK `clientId: null ⇒ universal` documented inline.

### FLAG (low — do not block)
- **F1 · LOW · the `resolveAmount` test name oversells its coverage — "temporal, active-only" are asserted by NAME but never exercised.** `commissionRates.api.test.ts:131` is titled `resolveAmount: most-specific-client-wins, temporal, active-only` but the body only proves specificity (client ₹80 beats universal ₹50), fallback-to-universal, and unconfigured→null. It never inserts a **deactivated** row and asserts it's excluded, nor an **end-dated/future** row to prove the `effective_from<=now() AND (effective_to IS NULL OR effective_to>now())` predicate. The resolver code is correct on read, but the two hardest-to-get-right clauses (active-only, temporal) ride on the title, not an assertion. **FIX (cheap):** add two cases — deactivate the client row → resolver falls back to ₹50; revise so the ₹80 row is end-dated in the past → resolver returns the current row only. Not a blocker (the predicate is shared with the list view's `history` filter, which IS tested, and the EXCLUDE/index are proven by the create/revise tests).
- **F2 · LOW · `resolveAmount` is a forward-hook with zero production callers in 5a (tested, but inert).** It's the ONLY non-CRUD method and exists solely for slice 5b's billing read-model (ADR-0036 §4, doc-comment says so). This is honest deferred-seam design, NOT dead code — but it's the one line that isn't "config only," so flag it for visibility: until 5b wires it, it's exercised only by its own unit test. **Disposition: ACCEPT** — building the resolver with the table it resolves against is reasonable cohesion, it's tested, and the ADR explicitly names it as 5a's surface. **RATCHET:** 5b must (per ADR CARRY) snapshot the resolved amount at the billing moment rather than re-resolving at `now()`, since this resolver is deliberately current-time only.

### INFO
- **INFO-1 · SDK `money` max exactly matches the DB column — no silent-truncation gap.** `commissionRates.ts:41` `z.number().nonnegative().max(9999999999.99)` and the column `numeric(12,2)` both cap at 10 integer + 2 fractional digits, so an over-cap amount is rejected at the Zod boundary (400) rather than overflowing the column (which would be a DB 22003). The `CHECK (amount >= 0)` + `.nonnegative()` are belt-and-suspenders-aligned. The repo's `input.currency ?? 'INR'` is redundant with the Zod `.default('INR')` (service passes the parsed output) — harmless.
- **INFO-2 · scope/RBAC proven both directions; FK path mapped but untested.** Tests cover create-201/join-list, overlap-409, revise-versioning+stale-409, deactivate/reactivate OCC, resolver specificity/null, RBAC 403 on BOTH read+write via a FIELD_AGENT (lacks `masterdata.manage`), and input-400 on a bad-uuid userId. The `23503`→`INVALID_REFERENCE` branch (e.g. a `clientId` for a non-existent client, or a non-existent `userId` slipping past the uuid-shape check) is mapped but has no test — low value (FK is DB-enforced), note only. Migration auto-applies: `testDb.ts` globs the migrations dir so 0058 is in the template clone; suite is `describe.skipIf(!RUN)` so it no-ops without `DATABASE_URL` (matches the green evidence: api 631/632, the 1 red is the documented `assignable-users` load-flake, NOT this module).

### Carried forward
- **F1 (low): add the two missing `resolveAmount` assertions (deactivated-row-excluded, end-dated/temporal) so the test body matches its title.** Cheap, do before 5b leans on the resolver.
- **F2/RATCHET (→ slice 5b):** the resolver is `now()`-only by design; the engine slice that PERSISTS commission MUST snapshot the amount at the billing moment (ADR-0036 CARRY), not re-resolve. `resolveAmount` stays inert until 5b wires it.

**Bottom line:** PASS — clear to commit. A faithful, scope-honest config foundation: `commission_rates` is modelled exactly like `rates` (effective-dated + OCC `version` + GiST no-overlap EXCLUDE with the universal-as-`-1` coalesce + half-open range + `WHERE is_active` resolve index), reuses the existing `page.masterdata`/`masterdata.manage` gate with no new permission, and the resolver is most-specific-client-wins + `now()`-temporal + active-only returning null-when-unset (correct, not an error). Mirroring `rates` is the right call and is done cleanly, with the single deliberate divergence (no tx on `setActive`, because there's no history side-write to atomize — self-historizing) being correct. Scope is genuinely "config only, engine later": no billed-state, no invoice/payout, no v1-FUCA touch, openapi adds only the 5 paths, and the lone forward-hook (`resolveAmount`) is a tested-but-inert seam the ADR explicitly names as 5b's consumer — honest, not premature. Two low FLAGs, neither blocking: the `resolveAmount` test title claims "temporal, active-only" coverage its body doesn't assert (add two cases), and that same resolver has no production caller in 5a (accept — cohesive deferred seam, ratchet the 5b snapshot-at-billing-moment per the ADR CARRY).

## 2026-06-16 — slice-5b commit review (ADR-0036 billing & commission model — the per-case Billing & Commission READ-MODEL; NEW `billing` module [repository/service/controller/routes + api.test] + NEW `0059_billing_view_perm.sql` + `@crm2/access` `BILLING_VIEW` (MANAGER+BACKEND_USER+meta) + `@crm2/sdk` `billing.ts` (+index/client/client.test) + app mount + openapi; working tree, UNCOMMITTED) — VERDICT: **BLOCK** (1 BLOCK, 0 FLAG, 2 INFO)

Adversarial read of the new read-model against ADR-0036's five decisions, with a scope-honesty sweep (truly read-only/derived?), a rollup-correctness check, a fork-vs-reuse check on the rate ladder, and an authorization sweep across ALL THREE mounted routes — not just the two the shipped tests exercise. The aggregate/lines model is correct, the rate ladder is byte-faithful to `cases/repository`, scope is genuinely derived (no billed-state), and the perm seed mirrors the prior idiom. **But the export route is gated on the wrong permission**, opening a real privilege gap on the most sensitive data in the slice (agent compensation). Blocking on that one route.

### BLOCK — `/cases/export` is gated `data.export` ONLY, NOT `billing.view` → a `billing.view`-denied role exfiltrates billing + commission data
`routes.ts:12` mounts `GET /cases/export` behind `authorize(PERMISSIONS.DATA_EXPORT)` while the two read routes (`/cases`, `/cases/:id/tasks`) are behind `authorize(PERMISSIONS.BILLING_VIEW)`. `authorize()` takes a SINGLE permission (`authorize.ts:23`, no AND-compose), so the export is gated solely on `data.export`. Per the DB seed (`0033_roles.sql:65-73`) **TEAM_LEADER holds `data.export` but NOT `billing.view`** — so a TEAM_LEADER who is correctly 403'd on `/cases` and `/cases/:id/tasks` gets **200 on `/cases/export`** and receives the full `BILLING_EXPORT_COLUMNS` set: caseNumber, client, product, **billTotal, commissionTotal** — the exact agent-compensation figures the ADR (D3) calls "more sensitive than rate cards" and the slice deliberately restricts to billing operators. **PROVEN EMPIRICALLY**, not merely reasoned: a throwaway probe test (TEAM_LEADER header on `/api/v2/billing/cases/export?format=csv&mode=all`) returned **status 200** (probe added + run against real Postgres, then removed; tree clean). The shipped `billing.api.test.ts` asserts the 403 gate on `/cases` and `/cases/:id/tasks` (test 4) but NEVER probes `/cases/export` — the gap rode in precisely because the perm test stopped at the two list routes.
  - **Why this is BLOCK not FLAG:** it's a live IDOR-class authorization bypass on compensation data, reachable by a real seeded role (TEAM_LEADER), through a route this very slice mounts. The list-route 403s give a false sense that the surface is gated; export silently isn't. Export is the higher-leverage exfil path (bulk, `mode=all`), so gating it MORE weakly than the row read is exactly backwards.
  - **Note the prior-art trap:** `rates/routes.ts:13` and `cases/dedupe-search/export` also gate export on `data.export` alone — but those are SAFE because their list routes are gated on `page.masterdata` / `dedupe.view`, perms whose holders ALSO hold `data.export` (no holder-set asymmetry). Copying that idiom into billing is the defect: here the list gate (`billing.view`) and the export gate (`data.export`) have DIFFERENT holder sets (TEAM_LEADER is in the second, not the first), so the pattern that's benign elsewhere leaks here.
  - **FIX (small, surgical):** gate `/cases/export` on `billing.view` (it is, after all, the billing read-model exported). Either change line 12 to `authorize(PERMISSIONS.BILLING_VIEW)` (export already requires no separate capability that `billing.view` holders lack — both grantees, MANAGER+BACKEND_USER, also hold `data.export`), or chain both guards if the design intent is "billing.view AND data.export". Then add the missing regression: TEAM_LEADER → `/cases/export` 403 (the assertion that would have caught this), alongside the existing `/cases` 403.

### ADR-0036 fidelity (the lens) — otherwise honored
- **D4 · derived now, engine later — scope-honest.** No billed-state persisted: the module is pure SELECT (repo has only `listCases`/`caseVisible`/`caseTasks`, all read), no `case_tasks.billed`/`billed_at`, no invoice/GST/payout, no migration beyond the perm seed (`0059` is a 2-row `role_permissions` INSERT, nothing else). Amounts are COMPUTED at read time via two LATERALs. The only "write" in the diff is the perm row. ✓
- **D1 · two amount sources.** `RATE_LATERAL` reuses the EXACT `rates` ladder from `cases/repository.ts:138-148` (verified line-by-line: same `client_id/product_id/verification_unit_id/is_active` predicate, same `effective_from<=now() AND (effective_to IS NULL OR effective_to>now())` temporal, same 5-tier `ORDER BY (location_id = ct.area_id) … DESC NULLS LAST … LIMIT 1` — only addition is surfacing `r.amount::float8 AS bill_amount`; the ladder logic is NOT forked). `COMMISSION_LATERAL` follows the rate lateral (so it can reference resolved `rt.rate_type`) and resolves `commission_rates` most-specific-client-wins (`ORDER BY cmr.client_id DESC NULLS LAST`) + active + `now()`-temporal + `(client_id IS NULL OR client_id=cs.client_id)` — identical idiom to 5a's `resolveAmount`. ✓
- **D2 · eligibility = ANY completed task.** `WHERE ct.status = 'COMPLETED'` is the sole eligibility predicate (no role/field-only filter); commission `LEFT JOIN LATERAL` → null when the assignee has no matching rate, NOT an exclusion (test 2 proves bill=100 still resolves with commission=null). ✓
- **D5 · outcome-independent.** No `verification_outcome` reference anywhere in the module. ✓

### Rollup correctness — verified
- **Count vs items grain is correct.** The count query uses `count(DISTINCT cs.id)::int` (pagination total = number of CASES); the items query `GROUP BY cs.id …` with `count(*)::int AS completed_task_count` (tasks per case). Since both LATERALs are `LIMIT 1` LEFT JOINs, the row fan-out is exactly 1 row per `case_tasks` row, so `count(*)` = completed-task count and `SUM(rt.bill_amount)`/`SUM(com.commission_amount)` are exact (no double-count from the lateral). `COALESCE(SUM(...),0)::float8` → unset commission rolls to 0 at the case grain while the line shows null — matches the SDK doc-comments (line: "null when…"; total: "unconfigured ⇒ 0") and test 2 (`commissionTotal===0`, line `commissionAmount===null`). ✓
- **Sort safety.** `o.sortColumn` is interpolated raw into `ORDER BY` but is whitelisted through `BILLING_PAGE_SPEC.sortMap` in the service (resolvePage maps client keys → fixed column strings); aggregate aliases (`bill_total`, `commission_total`, `completed_task_count`) are valid PG ORDER BY targets and `last_completed_at`/`cs.case_number`/etc. land pre-aggregation or as group keys. Tie-break `, cs.id ${order}` is deterministic. ✓
- **Scope predicate.** `caseScopePredicate` delegates to the shared `composeScopePredicate(..., 'CASE')` with a case-grain leg (`cs.created_by = ANY($N) OR EXISTS(… case_tasks ct.assigned_to = ANY($N))`); `$N` is `$K::uuid[]` against uuid columns — correct cast, single param reused twice in one fragment (valid PG). `''` (SA/ALL) → no filter. Defence-in-depth behind the `billing.view` gate; `caseVisible` reuses the same predicate for the lines 404-guard (test 4: absent uuid → 404, IDOR-safe; non-uuid → 400 via the controller `UUID_RE`). ✓

### Mirroring the platform idioms — clean
PageSpec/resolvePage/buildPage, the export `ExportColumn`/`resolveExport`/`writeExport` plumbing, the controller try/next + `parseCaseId` uuid-guard, and the SDK `pageQueryToParams`/`reqBlob('billing/cases', r)` shape all match the established `rates`/`cases` patterns. Perm seed `0059` is byte-faithful to `0056_task_revoke_perm.sql` (forward-only, idempotent `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`, mirrors `@crm2/access ROLE_PERMISSIONS`, no separate `permissions` catalog table — `0033` confirms `role_permissions` has no FK to a catalog). `BILLING_VIEW` added to PERMISSIONS + MANAGER/BACKEND_USER + PERMISSION_META (group 'Billing') consistently; `billing.ts` is type-only (0% coverage is expected, no runtime code).

### INFO
- **INFO-1 · evidence re-verified green locally.** typecheck PASS across all 8 workspace projects (`pnpm -r typecheck`); SDK 110/110 (`billing.ts` 0% = type-only, expected); billing API **4/4 PASS** against a real migrated Postgres (template-clone harness; `describe.skipIf(!RUN)`). The documented rotating multi-file load-flake (this run's red was elsewhere) is not in this module. The rollup E2E numbers in the brief (billTotal=150/commission=40/count=1, lines ORIGINAL/LOCAL) are consistent with the test assertions (100+30 in the seeded test; the :4000 run used different rate seeds).
- **INFO-2 · the `billing.generate` perm (MANAGER, `0033`) remains unused by any route** — pre-existing (not introduced here), a forward-hook for the deferred invoice-generation engine. Not this slice's concern; note only, do not touch.

### Carried forward
- **BLOCK→must-fix:** gate `/cases/export` on `billing.view` (or chain both guards) + add the TEAM_LEADER→`/cases/export` 403 regression. Re-run the api suite after.
- **RATCHET (→ engine slice, from 5a):** these LATERALs resolve at `now()`; the slice that PERSISTS billing/commission must snapshot the amount at the billing moment (ADR-0036 CARRY), not re-resolve.

**Bottom line:** BLOCK — one route fix away from PASS. The read-model itself is excellent: scope-honest (pure SELECT, zero billed-state, only-new-write is a 2-row perm seed), the rate ladder is byte-faithful to `cases/repository` (no fork), the commission lateral mirrors 5a's resolver, the count-vs-group rollup grain is exact (`count(DISTINCT cs.id)` for pagination, `count(*)`+`COALESCE(SUM)` per case under LIMIT-1 laterals → no fan-out double-count), null-commission rolls to 0 at the case grain correctly, and scope + IDOR guards (404 out-of-scope, 400 non-uuid) hold. **The blocker is narrow and proven, not theoretical:** `/cases/export` is gated `data.export` ONLY while the list routes are gated `billing.view`; because TEAM_LEADER holds the former but not the latter (per the DB seed), a role correctly 403'd on `/cases` gets **200 on `/cases/export`** (empirically confirmed against real Postgres) and exfiltrates the per-case bill + agent-commission totals — the slice's most sensitive data, leaked through its bulk path, gated more weakly than the row read. The `rates`/`dedupe` export-on-`data.export` idiom is safe only because there the list and export gates share a holder set; billing breaks that assumption. Fix = gate export on `billing.view` (both grantees also hold `data.export`, so no capability is lost) + add the missing TEAM_LEADER→export 403 test that would have caught it. Everything else clears.

## 2026-06-16 — slice-5c commit review (ADR-0036 billing & commission — the FRONTEND: two NEW pages over the already-audited 5a/5b APIs; NEW `features/billing/BillingPage.tsx` + NEW `features/commissionRates/CommissionRatesPage.tsx` + `App.tsx` routes (`/billing`, `/admin/commission-rates`) + `Layout.tsx` nav + e2e `a11y.spec.ts`/`viewport.spec.ts`; working tree, UNCOMMITTED) — VERDICT: **FLAG** (0 BLOCK, 1 FLAG-med, 2 INFO)

Adversarial read of both new pages against ADR-0036, the established DataGrid/MasterDataCrud/accordion conventions, hooks-rules correctness, and — the core ask — whether the page perm gates faithfully MIRROR the server gates (no false sense of access). The pages are clean, idiomatic, and the gates mirror the server exactly. **But the Commission Rates page wires a bulk Activate/Deactivate toolbar against backend routes that do not exist** — the bulk buttons 404 → "Bulk update failed." That's a shipped-but-broken control, not a security or data-integrity hole, so it FLAGs (med), not BLOCKs. Everything else clears.

### Page gates MIRROR the server — verified both pages, both directions
- **BillingPage gates `billing.view`** (`BillingPage.tsx:148`, return AFTER all hooks). Server: ALL THREE billing routes — `/cases`, `/cases/:id/tasks`, **and `/cases/export`** — are `authorize(PERMISSIONS.BILLING_VIEW)` (`billing/routes.ts:18-20`). The 5b BLOCK (export gated `data.export`-only → TEAM_LEADER exfil) **is FIXED**: export now shares the list's `billing.view` audience, and the FE export button (`apiExport('/api/v2/billing/cases/export…')`) therefore hits a route whose gate matches the page's own gate — no FE/server gate skew. Nav: `Layout.tsx` "Billing & Commission" → `/billing` perm `billing.view`. ✓
- **CommissionRatesPage gates `masterdata.manage`** (`CommissionRatesPage.tsx:240`, return AFTER all hooks). Server: ALL FIVE commission-rate routes (`/`, `POST /`, `/:id/revise`, `/:id/activate`, `/:id/deactivate`) are `authorize(PERMISSIONS.MASTERDATA_MANAGE)` (`commissionRates/routes.ts:14-18`) — both READ and WRITE on `masterdata.manage`, exactly as ADR-0036 D3 mandates (compensation data, SA-only, deliberately NOT the broader `page.masterdata` audience that `rates` reads allow). Nav: `Layout.tsx` "Commission Rates" → `/admin/commission-rates` perm `masterdata.manage`. ✓
- **Gate is defence-in-depth, server is the real gate.** The `has()` helper is byte-identical to the established convention (`!!user && (user.grantsAll === true || (user.permissions ?? []).includes(perm))`, same as `DedupePage.tsx:44-45`) — it reads the JWT-derived perms the server itself issued, never invents access. Page gate + nav-hide are cosmetic; the API authorize() is authoritative. No false-positive access path. ✓

### Hooks-rules — correct on both pages
Every hook (`useAuth`, `useState`, `useQuery`/`useMutation`/`useQueryClient`, `useMemo`) runs UNCONDITIONALLY before the perm-gate `return` (Billing L148, Commission L240) — no conditional-hook violation, no early-return-before-hooks. `BillingCaseLines` (accordion lazy-load) and `CommissionRateDialog` (create/revise) are separate components mounted conditionally, so their own hooks are unconditional within their lifecycle — correct. ✓

### FLAG — MED · the Commission Rates page ships a bulk Activate/Deactivate toolbar with NO backend route behind it → 404 on use
`CommissionRatesPage.tsx:261-268` sets `selectable` + `bulkActions={(sel) => <BulkStatusActions selection={sel} basePath={'/api/v2/commission-rates'} queryKey={'commission-rates'} />}`. `BulkStatusActions.tsx:41` POSTs to **`${basePath}/bulk-${action}`** i.e. `POST /api/v2/commission-rates/bulk-activate` | `/bulk-deactivate`. **Those routes do not exist.** The commission-rates router (`commissionRates/routes.ts`, slice 5a) declares ONLY `/:id/activate` and `/:id/deactivate` — single-row, integer `:id`. `/bulk-activate` is a one-segment path that cannot match `/:id/activate` (two segments), and the controller (`commissionRates/controller.ts`) has NO `bulkActivate`/`bulkDeactivate` method (only list/create/revise/activate/deactivate); service/repository have no `bulk*` either. So the bulk buttons → 404 → `BulkStatusActions` catch → "Bulk update failed. Please try again."
  - **Why this slipped:** `BulkStatusActions` is proven against the `rates` module, which DOES declare `/bulk-activate` + `/bulk-deactivate` + `c.bulkActivate`/`c.bulkDeactivate` (`rates/routes.ts:29-30`). 5c copied the `rates` page's `selectable`+`BulkStatusActions` idiom but the 5a commission backend never shipped the bulk pair (the 5a audit above lists only single activate/deactivate; bulk was never in scope). The browser-verify EVIDENCE exercised create + grid + single revise — it did NOT click bulk Activate/Deactivate, so the dead toolbar wasn't caught live.
  - **Why FLAG not BLOCK:** it fails SAFE — a 404 with a user-visible error toast, no data mutation, no perm bypass, no security/integrity consequence (contrast 5b's BLOCK which leaked compensation data). The toolbar only appears once rows are ticked. Single-row Revise (the dialog) AND create both use REAL routes (`/:id/revise`, `POST /`) and are functional + browser-verified. The page is usable; one secondary control is inert.
  - **FIX (pick one):** (a) ADD `POST /bulk-activate` + `/bulk-deactivate` (+ `c.bulkActivate`/`bulkDeactivate` + service, mirroring `rates`) to the 5a commission backend, gated `masterdata.manage`, with a bulk OCC test — preferred, since the page already promises bulk; OR (b) drop `selectable`+`bulkActions` from `CommissionRatesPage` (users deactivate one row at a time via a per-row action, like the existing Revise button) — smaller, ships the FE truthfully. Either way: don't leave a button that 404s.

### ADR-0036 fidelity (the lens) — honored on the FE
- **D1/D2 surfaced correctly.** Billing grid shows bill + commission per case; the accordion (`BillingCaseLines`, lazy `GET /cases/:id/tasks`) shows per-task lines + a Case-total row; `money(null) ⇒ '—'` renders unconfigured commission as a dash (NOT 0, NOT an error) at the LINE grain, while the case-total sums treat null as 0 (`l.commissionAmount ?? 0`) — matches 5b's documented grain (line null / total 0). Eligibility messaging "over completed tasks" matches D2; no `verification_outcome` reference (D5). ✓
- **D3 surfaced correctly.** Commission page presents per-user `(user, rateType, client[blank=universal], amount, effectiveFrom)` create + amount/effectiveFrom-only revise (user/rateType/client `disabled` on revise — correct, those are the no-overlap identity columns); "Universal (all clients)" for null clientId; OCC version threaded through revise (`version: row.version`) with a dedicated STALE_UPDATE→"reload and retry" message. SUPER_ADMIN-only framing in the page subtitle. ✓
- **Scope honesty.** Pure consumption of 5a/5b — `git status` shows ONLY the two new page dirs + App/Layout/2 e2e specs. No backend change, no new SDK, no billed-state, no invoice/payout/GST creep. ✓

### INFO
- **INFO-1 · FE→server sort/filter keys all align (no silent no-op).** Billing: all 8 sortable column ids (caseNumber/client/product/status/completedTaskCount/billTotal/commissionTotal/lastCompletedAt) map 1:1 to `BILLING_PAGE_SPEC.sortMap`; `defaultSort="lastCompletedAt"` matches server default; the `clientId` toolbar select → server `toPosInt(rawQuery['clientId'])`; dateFilter `completedAt` → filterMap `completedAt` (date). Commission: `defaultSort="user"` matches server; dateFilters `createdAt`/`effectiveFrom` → filterMap (both date). No FE control fires a param the server ignores. No unused imports on either page (swept). ✓
- **INFO-2 · evidence re-verified locally: `pnpm --filter @crm2/web typecheck` PASS (clean tsc --noEmit).** The brief's verify-green (typecheck 8/8, web build, api 636/636, sdk 110/110) and browser-verify on :5273 (Billing CASE-000030 ₹150/₹40 + accordion lines + client filter; Commission grid + UI-driven create AC1 SMOKE/OGL/₹60 persisted; 0 console errors) are consistent — BUT note the browser pass did not include the bulk path (see FLAG). e2e a11y/viewport specs add both routes (viewport marks Commission `primary: /New/` — correct, the create button exists; Billing has no primary, correct). ✓

### Carried forward
- **FLAG→fix before/with merge:** the Commission Rates bulk Activate/Deactivate toolbar has no backend route — either add `/bulk-activate`+`/bulk-deactivate` to the 5a commission module (mirror `rates`, gate `masterdata.manage`, +OCC test) OR remove `selectable`/`bulkActions` from the page. Add a smoke that actually exercises the chosen path.
- **RATCHET (→ engine slice, from 5a/5b):** these views resolve amounts at `now()`; the slice that PERSISTS billing/commission must snapshot at the billing moment (ADR-0036 CARRY). The FE just displays; no FE change needed.

**Bottom line:** FLAG — usable pages, one inert control. The core ask is satisfied: both page perm gates MIRROR the server exactly (Billing `billing.view` ↔ all 3 routes incl. the now-fixed export; Commission `masterdata.manage` ↔ all 5 routes, read+write, per ADR D3), the gate return is correctly AFTER all hooks on both pages, the `has()` helper is the established JWT-perm convention (cosmetic gate, server authoritative — no false sense of access), and FE sort/filter keys align 1:1 with the server PageSpecs (no silent no-ops). ADR-0036 is surfaced faithfully: null commission → "—" at line grain / 0 at case-total grain, revise disables the identity columns + threads OCC version, scope is pure 5a/5b consumption with zero backend creep. The one defect: the Commission page copied the `rates`-page `selectable`+`BulkStatusActions` idiom, but the 5a commission backend never shipped the `/bulk-activate`/`/bulk-deactivate` pair `rates` has — so bulk Activate/Deactivate POSTs 404 and shows "Bulk update failed." It fails safe (error toast, no mutation, no perm/data hole) and single-row Revise + create both work, so it's a med FLAG (ship-a-broken-button), not a BLOCK. Add the two bulk routes (preferred — the page promises bulk) or drop the bulk toolbar; either way exercise the chosen path before relying on it.

## 2026-06-16 — slice-5d commit review (ADR-0036 billing — Pipeline billable/commissionable VIEW; tasks `billable`+`billAmount`+`commissionAmount` derived on the Pipeline list + `commissionable` stat/bucket + shared `platform/billing/laterals.ts` reused by billing & tasks repos + FE Pipeline Bill Amt/Commission cols + Commissionable bucket; 7 files M + 1 new helper; working tree, UNCOMMITTED) — VERDICT: **FLAG** (0 BLOCK, 1 FLAG-med, 2 INFO)

Adversarial read against ADR-0036's frozen decisions (D1 two-source/no-fork, D2 ANY-completed-bills + null-commission≠exclusion, D3 comp-data more sensitive than rate cards, the now()-resolves/no-billed-state RATCHET), the 5b export-comp-leak lesson, lateral fan-out integrity, the billing-gate plumbing across list/stats/export, and a scope-honesty + surgical-changes sweep. The billing feature is correct and scope-honest. **But the edit dropped an unrelated `assignedTo` filter on the export path — a collateral regression (Karpathy surgical-changes violation), caught only because I diffed exportData against HEAD; `pnpm verify` 643/643 missed it (no export test covers assignedTo).**

### FLAG-med — `assignedTo` filter REGRESSED on `tasks/export` (collateral, NOT a billing defect)
`service.ts:185-191` (`exportData`'s `repo.list` call) no longer passes `assignedTo`. At HEAD it was present (`git show HEAD:.../tasks/service.ts:139` → `...(d.assignedTo !== undefined ? { assignedTo: d.assignedTo } : {})`). The 5d diff (the `-` at diff line 564) **removed that exact line and replaced it with the two new billing spreads** (`commissionable`/`billing`) → `assignedTo` fell out. The list (service.ts:125) and stats (service.ts:162) paths still carry it; only export lost it.
- **Impact:** `GET /api/v2/tasks/export?assignedTo=<uuid>` now ignores the assignee filter → exports ALL scope-visible tasks instead of that assignee's; export ≠ the filtered list the user sees. **NOT a security/scope leak** (the scope predicate still applies — no out-of-scope rows), purely correctness/UX.
- **Why it slipped:** zero export test exercises `assignedTo` (only the CSV-header test exists); the new 5d tests don't cover it either.
- **FIX (one line, surgical):** re-add `...(d.assignedTo !== undefined ? { assignedTo: d.assignedTo } : {})` to the exportData repo.list call + a regression: `export?assignedTo=<uuid>` → only that assignee's rows.

### ADR-0036 fidelity + the billing slice — CLEAR
- **D2 honored.** `billable = (ct.status = 'COMPLETED')` (repo.ts:78); commission null ≠ exclusion — the 5DB test proves an unpaid completed task still bills (₹100, commission null) and is excluded only from the *commissionable* bucket (`com.commission_amount IS NOT NULL`, repo.ts:131,197). Null-when-unset is correct, not a failure.
- **D3 comp-gate honored + the 5b export-leak class AVOIDED.** Amounts gated by `canViewBilling` (controller.ts:36-38 = `grantsAll || permissions.includes(BILLING_VIEW)`; `req.auth.grantsAll/permissions` populated by `enrichAuth`). Server authoritative — service nulls amounts, returns `commissionable=0`, ignores the commissionable filter for non-holders (service.ts:128-129,189-190); repo hard-guards `commissionable = billing && !!o.commissionable` so the `com.`-referencing predicate can never reach WHERE without its lateral in FROM. **Export does NOT leak comp data** (contrast the 5b BLOCK): `/export` is route-gated `data.export` only, BUT bill/commission columns are gated inside `taskExportColumns(canViewBilling)` (service.ts:449-473) → a `data.export`-holding TEAM_LEADER (lacks billing.view) exports WITHOUT the money columns. 5b lesson applied. FE gate (PipelinePage.tsx:66) cosmetic mirror only.
- **D1 no-fork.** Rate+commission laterals extracted byte-identical to `platform/billing/laterals.ts`, reused by billing/repository.ts AND tasks/repository.ts — kills the kickoff-flagged dup; the ⚠ doc-comment correctly flags the surviving cases/repository correlated-subquery copy as needing mirror.
- **Lateral integrity / no perf regression.** Both laterals `LIMIT 1` LEFT JOIN; list is row-grain (no SUM/GROUP) → 1:1, no double-count. COUNT/stats stay lateral-free over TASK_FROM unless commissionable is active (`countFrom` switch). Existing buckets unaffected.
- **Scope-honest + RATCHET respected.** Pure read/derived, NO persisted billed-state (grep clean), resolves at now() — engine slice still owns snapshot-at-billing-moment (5a/5b CARRY). Change set = exactly 7 files + the new helper; no invoice/payout/GST/mobile creep.

### INFO
- **INFO-1 (→Performance):** stats now runs 2 queries for billing.view holders (base aggregate + isolated COMPLETED-prefiltered commissionable count) vs 1 before; base stays lateral-free. Acceptable.
- **INFO-2:** API doesn't enforce bucket mutual-exclusivity (`?status=PENDING&commissionable=1` → ANDs to empty). Harmless, consistent with existing status+outOfTat coexistence; FE enforces in selectBucket.

### Disposition
- **FLAG→must-fix before commit:** restore the `assignedTo` line in exportData (service.ts:185-191) + add the `export?assignedTo` regression test. One-line revert of collateral damage; billing feature is otherwise PASS-grade.
- **RATCHET (carried from 5a/5b):** these views resolve at now(); the slice that PERSISTS billing/commission must snapshot at the billing moment.
- **OPEN (carried):** 5c Commission-Rates bulk Activate/Deactivate toolbar still 404s (add `/bulk-activate`+`/bulk-deactivate` or drop the toolbar) — unrelated to 5d, still outstanding.

**Bottom line:** FLAG — one-line revert away from PASS. The Pipeline billing VIEW is faithful and scope-honest: billable = COMPLETED (D2), null-commission bills-but-not-commissionable (D2), comp amounts gated by billing.view across list/stats/export with the server authoritative and the 5b export-leak class designed out (money columns gated inside the export manifest, not just the route), the rate/commission laterals shared not forked (D1), lateral fan-out exact, no persisted billed-state (RATCHET intact), and the change set is exactly in-scope. The single defect is collateral, not billing: the edit that inserted the two billing spreads into exportData's repo.list call also deleted the adjacent `assignedTo` spread, so task export silently ignores the assignee filter (export ≠ list). It fails safe (scope predicate still bounds the rows — no leak), but it's a real regression that 643/643 missed because no export test covers assignedTo. Restore the one line + add the regression, then this is clear to commit.
